Occasionally there is a link that comes under the tongue or by nature, which does not occur naturally; or by accident of a healed wound; and the operation is such that you open the mouth of the patient, hold his head in your hand, lift the tongue; then take hold of the nervous link wide enough so that the tongue is dislocated from its position, and if there is hardness or swelling, and it is due to a wound, push the incision and seize it widely; and make sure that the cut is not too deep, for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done this, lift the area with rosewater and linen, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and keep the patient from healing.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if bleeding occurs, place vitriol powder on it; and if the wound bleeds again, cauterize it with slow-burning cautery (lentiginout), which is good for this purpose; then treat it with another cure until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see the swelling becoming pale or black or hard and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it because it is a chancre; if it is declining towards blenchor and there is moisture, throw the forceps and use a thin spatula to deliver it from both sides. If it does not heal at your treatment, apply vitriol powder until it heals completely. Then raise the swelling with cold water and vinegar, and cure it with other treatments until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	Abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes inside the throat come objects called "godath," which are correctly called almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they are not healed, beware: if it is a hard abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the reason of bleeding; but let it be until it turns black, and then you will cut it, or it will break by itself; and if it is white in color and the root is thin, prepare the instrument to cover it, but first make sure that the abscess pus has settled down and been soothed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit in the sun, and his shoulder should be placed on a pillow, and open his mouth wide, and the sergeant grasps the tongue between his hands, and presses it down onto the instrument, thus forming this shape; and let it be made of silver or thin brass like scissors.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And you press the tongue to this whole instrument and see the abscess, then take the awl and poke it into the almond, and pull it out upwards more than you can; and pull something from the cloth with it, then hit it on the instrument in this way, which looks like a hammer, and although the head is curved, one end to another, and they are very sharp, it is made of iron or copper.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, use pliers of this shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	Then take pliers of the following shape: and when you have gripped one of the almonds, grip the other in the same manner, and after incising, pour hot, sharp, and astringent liquids over the wound, and if bleeding occurs, pour more hot liquids or scorched pomegranate skins or myrtle leaves, and similar things until the blood is stopped; then cure it until it heals; sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat instead of the two almonds, so grip them as you would the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treat a woman with an abscess that is located within the throat, to be specific, an abscess of small size; and I had tightly closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not exhale due to the blocked passageway, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained in this state for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so high that it had been placed two fingers breadths inside the nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 Then I immediately stuck an onion into one nostril, then pulled it out, and a large piece of pus followed; next, I stuck the onion again into the other nostrils, opened the mouth, and pressed the tongue; afterwards, I stuck the onion into these abscesses, took a part of it, and nothing but a little blood came out; and thus the conduit of the throat was unblocked for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting off this abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing back again, filling the cavity that I had opened, until it became very large; then I tricked it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left these parts, and let God do with them what he would after me.
de l’uve	Of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When the arm descends towards the eye, and it has swollen and is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help at all, and you see that the abscesses are soothed, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and the one that is round and not long; and it is bloody or of pale color or black, then you must make an incision on it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger on the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its swelling and length, you must make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument mentioned before; then pierce the onion into the eye, and draw it out, and cut it at the two points that I have said in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And it is necessary that you not cover excess beyond the natural term; for if you do so more, it harms the voice and speech; and after incision, use what has been said in the incision of the two testicles, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 If the patient fears covering (it), then you must use an engine for the cauterization to alleviate fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the manner of cautery is sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And the patient places his head in your lap, and then you press the tongue against the instrument as has been said in the chapter of cautery, and hold it with hot and sharp force, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and use the handle of this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has hair or a tumor at the eye, apply the medicine with a scoop-shaped spoon, and place the instrument over all of the medicine on the eye; the patient lies on his side so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine without reaching the throat or nose, then hold your hand over all of the medicine and press it on the eye until you see the swelling and abscesses subsided and the pain caused by the medicine has been alleviated; then take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, insert the instrument into the canal above, so that the cotton sticks to the eye; repeat this process until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry for 4 or 5 days. If you need to start over with the cauterization of the medicine, restart it and after the cauterization, irrigate around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, clean what is around the medicine; then wash with cold water and treat with gargling until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more subtle than incision, or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calmander and yarrow and origanum and rue and chamomile and savory and similar herbs, and put them all together or some of these in .i. pot, and add ashes, and let it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot there should be .i. hair-like instrument according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And it should be silver or iron, and one of the heads pushed into the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is putrefied; afterwards, it often happens, until the eye dries up; and see that you do not do this at the beginning of the abscess's heat, for many things can happen; and do not do this except when the abscess's heat declines.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this instrument is not present, take a reed and put an eggshell crack in the patient's head so that the mouth does not become too hot; for the eggshell does not let the vapor harm the mouth, and it is a good cure combined with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens that bone or a spine of fish or something else gets stuck in the throat, so you must remove what you can see and press the tongue against the sun with all the instruments until you see movement; if it does not open by itself and remains lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit as soon as the meat is cooked in the stomach. Perhaps that will expel the stuck object through vomiting; or the patient should swallow a piece of sponge, a piece of cotton, a root of lettuce, or one morsel of dry bread; tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; when it reaches the location, it will stick, and you will draw it out; and if it does not come out due to what we have said, take .i. instrument made of wood according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the tip so that it can more easily enter the throat, and keep the head raised high; and watch that you do not touch the epiglottis, as the patient should not push it down or force the bone within; rather, it is better for the patient to push the instrument in, because they are pushed or the matter is loosened; if it is pushed down, or pulled out all the way, it should be equal throughout the length of the instrument until it is removed.
de la sansue de la gorge	and remove the saliva from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the remedy is the snake, as I said in the division, through the treatment of medicines; and when it does not help, then look at the patient's throat towards the sun, afterwards hold their tongue with the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the snake, draw it out with a very small pair of scissors or subtle pliers that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if that doesn't work, take a heated iron rod and put it in the patient's throat, then push or move the heated iron upwards several times.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And the patient should be kept wet all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a whole glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, then move it with your hand frequently; and as soon as the snake feels the water, it falls.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall as we have said, anoint the patient with asafoetida in the instrument that I mentioned for the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will heal quickly.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 The method of fumigation is that you take a pot with charcoal inside, and cover it with a perforated cloth in the middle, and put the head of the instrument in the opening; then pour your fumigation into it, and the patient places the back of their neck in their mouth, and closes their mouth so that no smoke escapes, but comes up to the nostrils instead; and now let it stay, and if it does not fall, repeat the fumigation many times; and the patient should endure thirst, eat salted and acidic foods, and drink no water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out with this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the instrument used to treat the nose, is such that when it can be seen, resembles curved pincers for entering into the throat; and resembles the nozzle of a syringe, and has an abrasive surface so that what it takes, it cannot lose; and here is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many things resembling abscesses are mentioned in this chapter, according to what is recalled here from one and the other in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision; and it is in two ways that one of them is similar, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is for the lungs in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 for abscesses of the head are different from those in the body, and the abscesses caused by the lung are different from those that come in joints, and each should have its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the swelling is measured according to its completion; and if there are those that must be pierced when they are ripe, but do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that come from joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when an abscess comes near to joints and is left until it is ripe around, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint may rot, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 If the abscess is near the main body of the member and you delay the puncture until it has ripened, it will harm the main member; or if the abscess is near the base, it should be pierced as soon as it has ripened; and you should not puncture an abscess without proper digestion, except when it is near the base, which cannot be pulled out, and is long inside, and there comes a fistula; and it cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time of perforation for the abscess that is ripe according to its completion, and it is when the pain is alleviated, and the disappearance of fever, and reduction of pain and redness, and swelling and shrinkage of the abscess head, and other signs; and you should make the perforation site lower than the abscess, and where it has opened up; and let the perforation be long along the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, in jointures, at nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no ploughing.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that droop, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a hard place, it is worth letting the puncture remain until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce before that, the body will be lengthened with its fluid, and it will fill with much filth; and perhaps the lips harden and it becomes deeply infected by it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And you should make small abscesses, small punctures; and large abscesses, large punctures, and many slits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to be careful, and cover; when it has become like a linen cloth, and is softened, it is necessary to do as with babies: and if there are those that have been slit into three angles, and if there are those from which one covers like the branch of myrtle, as abscesses in joints; and if there are those where a round cut is made, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 He who has no head, like an abscess superficial, it should be pierced completely; and when the abscess is large and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out a part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out nothing improperly; do this repeatedly, slowly, as much as necessary, until the pus is all drawn; likewise, if the patient is of weak vitality, or a woman carrying, or small children, or elderly people decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 Sometimes the pus jolts out with discharge, by chance the patient dies, and you should not worry about it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, be extremely careful with this chapter, and when you have pierced the abscess, squeeze out the wound, and look to see if the wound from the abscess is small; if it is a large hole, bring threads of linen or old cotton; if it is a big abscess, and there is a lot of pus, you must insert a thread in each one so they come together; if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin and shaved around it, fill it with old cotton or linen dressing without moisture, tie it up until the third day; then open it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold water and a cloth, wet the cloth, and put it on the place, pressing it several times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the bleeding continues, bring governance and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is during winter, and the place or abscess is very nervous, then you must put hot towels and cloths moistened with wine and oil on top of it; but if it is summer, and the place is fatty, then you must put wet towels and cloths on top of it, or cold ones made of wine and oil, for two days, as we have said; then open the abscess, drain it, and heal it until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	This must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how to proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 For small abscesses at the head, there are methods that we know of, which are wrapped in cloths, as is the case with a juniper berry, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are fat and such-like ones with moisture, as well as blisters; and there are those that are hard and stony at the edge, and there is no doubt that the arteries do not oppose it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of the cut is that you explore with every instrument that is called "intermissoire", from which the form follows, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 If it contains moisture, they make it through the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is emptied, scrape off the skin that contains it, because it returns again if nothing is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if it is available; if not, in water and oil, and apply it to the wound, leaving it until the next day; and this will heal those that are delayed by night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then continue with the cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know it does not stay in place; then treat the wound with suitable ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 If the abscess is full of pus, squeeze it in this manner, along its length; and throw out your onions, and peel off all its skin, and put all your treatment to draw away the pus where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do as I told you before.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And do the same with the abscess if it is hard, and cut and treat as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 Cut above the hard abscess and moisturize it, for it will be easier, since there is a little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if in any of these abscesses or head there is no moisture, as was the abscess that I cut open from an old woman's head; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had pierced it with anything, one would have made a wound like from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses or heads coming from children's heads and roots of the ears, one should open them always as much as possible, to allow pus to drain; and treat them as necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Often this abscess appears at the neck, under the jawbones, in angles, and sometimes it occurs elsewhere on the body, and they are large and connected to each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 Each scrofula is properly within its side, as the lymph node and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similarities with these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 Some contain moisture, and some are malicious ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In the one that you see with a good disposition on the surface and is similar to the color of the body, silent in all parts and is neither at the neck artery nor the conduit, nor is it hollow; then you must cut through it from above, peel off each part, and put the two ends of the cautery as close as possible to each other, if you have them, as we have said in abscesses of the head; pull it gently and carefully, ensuring that you do not cover the nerve or the vein, and be careful not to use a spatula or cut too deeply, so that the hand does not slip, and do not look too far ahead, lest you cover what should not be covered.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not let you go, put vitriol powder into the wound or some powders that stop blood, and hold the wound; leave it until the abscess is appeased and the wound becomes soft and begins to suppurate.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 When the wound has stopped bleeding, return to your work until you are finished; then look for any small scrofula spots and cut them and wash them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 If there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula spot, it is not necessary to cut that scrofula spot at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it hang down without harm; then use old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment on the wound and heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you excise the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you sew together the two edges of the wound, because there will be no excess remaining due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 It is necessary that you understand how to cover the root [of something], draw out the pus, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulas that have excess, pierce there where it becomes open; and pierce in such a way as the one mentioned above, on the edge, then introduce tweezers with ointment and similar things, so that it destroys what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply an ointment-infused char cloth until it heals.
de squinance	Inflammation or swelling
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the size of the throat but I never saw anyone do it in our land and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinancy, it is required that the cleft in the throat, called "epiglottis", be opened; and no aid should be given by these (people), for all the veins and the pormon of the sickness are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in two amandres (tonsils).
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pormon (throat), it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger of strangulation that comes from the swelling.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it below three circles or four small incisions across, between the second and third circles or according to the size of the incision, not in the cartilage; and such places are suitable for cutting the epiglottis that there is no cartilage present, and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is afraid, then it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat all along, then cuts the keyhole as long as it reaches the chin; and avoids the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then severs the cartilage, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the trachea that jumps through the broken place, and by the lack of voice; and leaves the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour has passed in which there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound with care, and sew it up entirely through the cartilage; then administer medications that cause healing until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi said that one should not do this until the throat is entirely stopped up, and the patient is pronounced dead, and his soul departs.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Therefore, press on the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, thus preventing death; and for this reason, the old would command to keep the wound open as long as the malice of the disease has passed, which passes in 3 or 4 days. And then they would command to sew up the wound and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 A young girl took the knife and stabbed herself in her throat, piercing part of the windpipe; I was called to heal her, but found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found blood coming from it, and knew that neither vein nor artery had burst, but the blood was flowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hastily sewed up the wound and healed it until she was well; nothing bad happened to the girl but her voice became hoarse, and she returned to her condition; for this reason, I say that in such a case of the epiglottis, have no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess with a yellowish color, and it is predominantly in women; and it is of two kinds: natural and accidental; where the natural one has no device.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 The accidental one is also of two kinds: the first kind resembles a fat pouch, and the second kind resembles an abscess that comes from an artery; there should be caution, and it should not be forced except in the case of small ones, and it must be thoroughly examined: if you find it like a fat pouch, and it is not opening at all, if you press it, as one presses fingers, and draw it to its full length, if there is any, and enclose it well, and cure it as necessary, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	From us (meaning the medical practitioners)
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways of ours are, which I shall tell you all their similarities; and now it is necessary that I say the entire difference between notch and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that discharge is heat and fever persisting, until the eruptions have passed, and the boils have matured; then the fever and heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 A notch has neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains the site, which is its own sac and is in accordance with the color of the body, and begins as a blister and becomes large; and there are two similarities, either fat or moist, and it is often colored as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the newt, that you examine and test first all the equipment called "entromissoire", according to its shape or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 The method of the incision of abscesses in our ways is that you take or more moist place than you find within the abscess, and turn your fingers bit by bit until you feel that the instrument has pierced through, then according to the size of the abscess; then draw out the contents, but beware that it does not burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs out from the abscess, let it be colored as I said for other abscesses; and if afterwards no moisture comes out at the opening, know that it is filled with pus, then make a cross incision, take hold of it with forceps, peel it gently on both sides and pull the skin where it lies carefully to remove it safely; if you cannot remove it safely, then remove it in pieces so nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 If nothing remains, the pus returns many times; if a little remains and it does not trouble you, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, hold the wound closed with hot things that ease abscesses, treat it with other remedies until it heals; if the abscess is large, cut it in two, treat the wound with what cures sores.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the veins are bleeding or other similar cases, use crushed vitriol and let it lie for 2 to 4 days until the wound dries up, allowing the blood vessels to heal; then return to bandaging that which remains unhealed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Behold the shapes of the stirrups, and they are of three kinds: large, medium and small; and there are three squares among them which are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are also three types: large, medium, and small, to surround abscesses with fistula; and they are similar to needles used for sewing violets, and they are made of citron wood, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and those with black handles are more experienced in encircling the corners of fistula; and they are also of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The forms of the cones are very similar, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and some cones have two bends in three ways; and some cones have three bends and are also of three types; and some cones have two bends, and cones with a single bend only, and they are also of three types; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The tips of these [things] are sharp and those that do not cut only from one side, from which we scrape the nerves, for this reason so as not to hit the vein or nerve; and these intromissoires are replied in many ways, so that the patient does not feel it at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you see; and none are used except for charnut [charred] places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and genitals, and similar places; and sometimes another instrument is used, resembling fistula scissors, according to this shape, for draining blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed at the site where the vein or artery bleeds, and sometimes they return according to this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them must do so according to this form from this line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Then scrape the fat, apply medicine to the wound in a soothing way, then bring together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it heals; and if the breast tilts downwards and is deformed due to its size, as happens with women, make it into two folds above, by two similar cuts; so that one is attached to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this form, from this line b to the line g; then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, remove the fat, and bring in what we have said about stitches and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure, until it heals; and if it does not heal, or the incision is not completely made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you should fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it softens the remaining fat and the wound, then treat it until it heals.
des apostemes des asselles	of the abscesses from the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	these abscesses coming from the buttocks are handled as hard scrofulas, or they have coats containing moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those containing moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b up to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the whole cavity in the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton, and treat it with an ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofulas, make them as we have said in cutting into scrofulas, and if it swells, apply fire cure as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	For the cutting of an artery...
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When the artery is wide and the skin above it is joined, it often occurs that abscesses develop, and the same thing happens with a swollen vein and an abscess; and if one recognizes it by the artery, the abscess extends deep within; and when you feel it with your fingers, it feels constricted; and when it is a vein, it swells and appears round; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, and especially when it is below the joints and at the angles and near the neck and in many other places, and it is large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, you must remove the iron cure and also the one at the head should be removed, and in the one who is swollen from an artery, make a cut through the skin along its length; then open the incision carefully and separate the artery from the tendons, as long as it is exposed; then insert an awl beneath it and pierce it up to the other side and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples; then press the area between the two tendons with an introducer until the blood stops flowing and the abscess is drained; then apply the cure that will stop bleeding, until the tendon heals; then treat the area with ointment as appropriate, until it is healthy; if the abscess is from the vein opening, you must dye your hand with what you can of the abscess along the entire skin, then insert an awl beneath the area that you hold in your hand, pierce it and have a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or the tendon of one of the two sides with threads; if you doubt that the threads will not protrude, insert another awl along the entire length of the abscess at the incision of the first awl and tie the threads in four places; then press the abscess until the excess is expelled, then press the excess fat and leave what is tied; then put a soft cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply cures of tents and ointments until it is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses from nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and the vein, so they come to nerves when they are struck or from excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens more often in shoulders and fingers and all joints where there are joints, and it is the greatest abscesses, and its color resembles the body's color, and it is found in many positions with pain; and when it is forced outwards, the patient feels pain, and it is not completely within the body, but under the skin; and it is silent all over, and does not go neither forwards nor backwards, neither up nor down, and the one who is in joints should not be covered with iron: by accident it may contract; and he who is on the head or on the forehead, let the skin be scraped with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and strike at its root; if it is large, suspend it on a lance and peel it off, then open and clean the wound and stitch it together until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	hanging large lumps
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes it happens in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots and large heads; and there are small and very large ones; I have seen people who had two bellies that were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had a narrow root, and were split open, and continually oozed moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I cut and found in one 18 pounds weight, and in the other 6 pounds, and the openings in the incision were such that you could see if the patient was moist, and the color of the arterial blood was white and moist with a thin root; if it is chopped at a large spatula, let there be fire cautery in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For at the thigh there often comes excessive bleeding, and if it floods, then you hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the iron incision, take a fine thread made of yarn, tie the ligature as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then tighten it, and do not stop tightening the thread of yarn until it stops the bleeding, and causes pain; and if the roots are large, be cautious when covering because of the stomach, but you can well cover half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and take care not to cover the knot which is of dark color and poor sensation and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess swollen, and I will come to the treatment of this scrofula later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil bursts
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of boils comes from cautery of a wound or a cut in the scrotum, as it happens in other routes, or from blood that leaks from veins or arteries as described before, or from wind; and if it is through the route of the scrotum and through the exit of the testicle, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, it is a light thing without pain, and has an open exit of diverse exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the outflow of the intestine, then it is more varied; and when pressed with the fingers, it sinks in, and then returns, and by chance if it is sutured, it increases greatly at the entrance of the bath and through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is light and easily pressed with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, the abscesses are large and hard, and are filled according to a certain quantity; and if it is due to wind, it is soothing to touch, and the operations require that you observe whether the appearance is due to blood from the artery or vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 It is necessary to let the healing take place.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 Because there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, you must instruct the patient to take hold of his anus, stretch it out straight, then sign all around the fecal matter; then command him to grasp it between your hands, then go around the area that you have signed with a spatula, then extend half of the abscess above the great spoon; then sew it around with a strong thread or cord made from strong silk firmly, and leave the sutures loose; then open half of the extended abscess over the suture, and insert your index finger, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught in the suture, unsew it, remove the intestine out of the abdomen; and if you find the bowel, take it with the spoon, and empty its superfluity; and if the artery opposes or the vein does, go around carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, insert four threaded filaments into them, and insert them around what you have made in a cross shape that you are piercing; then hold the abscess open with four leagues above the needles, and if you see any holes, remove the needles, and leave the area until it becomes dry, then cut off the dead flesh as necessary, and cure it as previously described; and drain any blood or moisture that you find, then cure the area.
dou chancre	two boils
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of boils, and how one should treat them with medicines, and how one should choose the cure of iron; and we shall say what a boil is like, and great caution in its care, and the ancients said that when boils are in a place where they can be shaved like boils that are on mamels, and in the thigh, and similar places, it should all be removed when it begins; and when it is large and old, it is not advisable to approach it, for I never knew anyone heal one; no one ever healed one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operation, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient once with black bile; then make him urinate if there is manifest retention, then cut open one boil to perform the operation; then pour your onions or boils, and shave the head of all parts, and remove everything without leaving anything; let the blood flow freely, and press well the place with your hand or something else, and if the flow of blood makes you against the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the wound is cauterized; then cure it with another treatment until it heals.
de ydropisie	From hydropisy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have said in the division that the resemblances of edema are similar to idropisie; and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs for each resemblance, and the treatment using medicines, and the one that is treated with iron: these are only blisters; no iron should be used in these two resemblances, namely tympanites and iposarche, because it is a deadly thing; therefore, when you treat this edema resemblance called "blisters" using medicines, and the treatment does not improve, observe if the patient is weak or has other diseases besides edema, such as abdominal swelling and similar things; do not use iron in that case because there is doubt; and if you see the patient strong and he only has edema, and he is neither too young nor too old, then proceed like this: lift the patient upright onto your hands, and let the minister press his abdomen pushing water to the lowest part of the bladder, then take the pointed spatula as shown below:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be incised through two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And let it be incised no deeper than it can reach up to the intestines when pushed in, and not pierce through; then check if the bile duct is connected towards the intestines: if so, you must cut above the third rib on the left side; and if it is due to liver disease, the incision should be to the left of the third rib; and if it is due to stone, it should be to the right, and the patient should not lie down on the incision so that excess fluids do not run into that weak area; then pierce the skin with the instrument, and push it in, and place your hand at the tip of the spatula as much as the thickness of a nail or more; then pierce the spatula until it reaches the level of eight, which is the bile duct, and pull it out, and push this instrument in the position shown:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it is similar to a silver needle, thin and made of thread or light wire, and has a small pointed tip; and on one side, three points; and two on the other side, and one on another; and the head is shaped like a quill pen, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes make with a pen:
