au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 On the handle above is the anguilliforme, so that when the instrument comes to the marrow, then press now on the instrument; empty it out then in the area that you should, for if you empty it too much at that hour, perhaps the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit due to the weapon or he falls down or approaches death; but empty according to its strength and as the patient's condition and pulse indicate; then take the instrument and stop the marrow, and it is held now by the caution that stops the perforation which is above the siphon, as I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then return the instrument on another day, if you see the patient suffering from this, and draw out a small amount of marrow; do this every day and be careful not to wait too long but only a little marrow.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt about the patient and let him have much water, cure him with burial or hot sand, and with much sweating or bathing in the sun, and anoint him with wine; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and the liver and the spleen after the extraction of water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born who have no foreskin or the foreskin is small or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 If it is necessary to pierce the spittle very thinly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 Then place the thin foreskin of pine wood over it and bind it and keep it like that for three or four days until he wants to urinate, then remove the foreskin, let him urinate, and then put it back; and it is not necessary in this case because the urine that comes out does not leave the foreskin closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 The patient whose ulcer is small, is treated with a poultice of linen, as we have said, it will open up.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those who do not have the ulcer in their place are bled, for no one is born whose ulcer is at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they raise their penis; and they cannot ejaculate due to the material that cannot reach the marris (the opening of the urethra), and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of work is that the patient lies on his back, his penis and scrotum should be exposed as much as possible, so that the foreskin can be pulled out as much as necessary; and take care to avoid bleeding which often occurs, and if it happens, apply a bandage to stop the bleeding and cure the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	The boils of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often this albath comes in the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly genitals; there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; you must take them once a week with a subtly thin instrument, scrape and clean them all, then put soft cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on them; then cure them with diaphinicon ointment until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the ulcer is malignant, with pus-like color and odor, you should apply a fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have burned it (the ulcer), and if the ulcer is on the penis and has both parts inside the skin and outside, you must first remove the ulcer that is inside; and when it is healed outside, heal it inside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you treat it together, the testicles of the penis are not always certain to not be pierced, and darkness and corruption appear in its length and around it; then it is necessary to cut away all that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster made of honey and flour which should be made from pomegranate rind and wheat, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding comes out, bring the lunar cautery as follows:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cauteries aid in the following way: for bleeding and corruption; and if the testicles of the penis are corrupted and retracted, it is necessary to bring or administer a catheter from the penis, and make the patient urinate; and when the hairs reach the tip of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or it happens due to injury or abscess, then it is necessary to shave it with an instrument, until the ligaments are loosened, and the testicles of the penis are released from all sides; and if this is a difficult thing to discuss, then it is necessary to shave it with a spatula at any point along the penis and the pubic hair; then press together well, and put a thin linen cloth dampened in cold water between them so that they do not touch again.
de la circoncision	circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the discontinuation of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this work according to our will and specifically on children, it is necessary that we perform the best and most delicate work for their salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not circumcise their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have it only because we acquired it through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the greatest part of masters and healers who performed circumcision around one day, and for adults and novices; however, it is dangerous because there are two layers, and in case one above is cut and left the other below remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now cover it with copper, and the pain is doubled; and at the amputation which is deep near the limb, the point of the knife may slip, spoiling the work, and many times it does not require amputation and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	In the amputation which is performed I have found the advantage of using wire in that the wires cut equally well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you press your hand, you should make an equal cut all through it; but the blade should be well straightened around the skin; and the method of the first operation is such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you do not pierce him except to tie the thread around the rod only, and afterwards let him enjoy in every possible way that you can; then make it lie straight between your hands, and tighten the forces between your hands or beneath your feet so that the child does not see, nor any instrument; then push your hand against the rod and blow or cut, and draw it up until the head of the rod is in; then clean it well of the filth that has gathered there, then tie the ligature with a double thread, then tie the other end to another ligament; and hold it by the second ligature at the thumb and the index finger, and strike between the two ligaments, then draw the knot quickly and pull the head of the rod; then let the blood flow freely, for that is the pus; and put powder on it and on the powder apply egg white stirred with a well-cooked rose water, and let it stay until the next day, and treat it with another treatment until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for cleansing is as follows: the two heads should be tender and sharp, and they should be as large as the thumb equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mundification is when the kidneys are incised within; therefore, you should stretch it with your fingernail, so that the incision becomes an abscess; and equalize it, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, take tweezers, and then equalize.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If they exceed three days, and that which is beneath the spermatic cord swells, let it be left until the abscesses calm down, and gently incise it; and equalize it as you can move it, and take care of the part of the spermatic cord, it will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the limb of things submerged in a wound with powder, as we have said or treated powders, and if it is equalized too much, it will go upwards, but it will not harm; then cure it as we have said, until it heals.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is caused by a stone, frozen blood, a boil, pus, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not relieved, and you see that the retention is due to a stone lodged in the bladder neck, then the patient should be bent over his knees; and the feet should be placed on the back, and he should extend his abdomen from the upper part of the back, and restrain the patient as much as possible; and then the bladder neck is compressed to express the stone above, so that the urine is relieved; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction using all the instruments called "syringe," of which this is the form: and it should be made of subtle silver, light cylinder shaped, like a bird's feather; and the cannula should be one and a half palms long, and it should be subtle at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the method of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, tie it to the head of a cotton or wool swab, and push the head of the thread into the syringe; cut off the excess of the swab and push it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and seat the patient on a chair, and anoint the bladder and penis with oil moistened with warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then fold the penis over towards the abdomen; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and make the patient feel as though they are urinating into an empty vessel, and this is not done according to this order unless the conduit through which it flows is twisted; then tie the thread all along the swab and the urine follows the swab, then extract it forcefully, and correct the urine; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is empty, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood come in the bladder, or pus is accumulated there, and you see it distill liquids and medicines, do everything with the instrument called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and if it has three openings: two of one side, and one of another, as you see; and the lews cheeks are such that the medicines should be so soft that they stop the worm without addition, if one can draw out the moisture, and push when necessary; and when you wish to throw your medicines into the bladder, place the head of the cestrum in the moisture, and draw along with it; if you draw out the moisture with the cestrum, and then forcefully push it back along; the moisture will enter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle clisterm which they use to clisterize the bladder: here it is.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is made of silver or iron, and the head is raised higher; and below the breast or the shoulders fall down; then take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture you have prepared to cleanse the bladder; then fold it between two breasts forming a good double thread, and heat the moistened part over the fire; then insert the head of the clistere into the wound, then hold your hand above the bladder with all the moisture coming out; until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the wound; and if you don't have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle, puncture it roundly; then push a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle like a thimble, fill it with oil, water, and moisture, and put it in the instrument; do as you have done with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the wound.
de la piere	From the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the methods of stone and its extraction with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone implanted in the eye and all the signs, and in which stone one should operate according to size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder happens more often to children, and this is a sign that the stone leaps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; it opens holes, and burns the patient's urinary organ, pierces it many times, and then ties it up; and from these leaps the foundation weakens; and the healing of children is light until they are four years old, but it is very severe in the elderly, and it is between middle age and old age for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those with large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, in order to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes hinders the seeking of the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and push downwards and move them towards underneath, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and sometimes rises up a little; then make him sit between your hands arranged, and his hands should be beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is completely declining downward; then press and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall by touching all over, you should anoint your hand with oil from the left, if the patient is weak, or heat it, if the patient is fully grown; and push it into its foundation, seeking for the stone, and when you feel it with your hand, remove it at the neck of the bladder; then press up on it and push it out where you see to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the servant to press on the bladder with his hand, and command him to stretch out his right hand upward, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the muscles in the area where the cutting is done; then insert the spatula covering it.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And between what is between the coccyx and the foundation, do not touch the middle but the left side of the navel; it should be straight above the stone, and your hand should be in place or at the foundation, and it should be carved through the middle so that it is wide by the exit, and narrow inside according to the size of the stone, not too large; by chance, the pressure on the hand that is at the foundation may cause it to jump out with effort; and know that there are many stones or angles and margins: if it is smooth to remove; and if it is soft, like a plum and round, the exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 To the one who has angles and swelling, make an incision larger; if it does not open by itself, you must force it with pliers resembling a chisel at the head, to press the stone so that it doesn't escape; or push underneath using a subtle crooked probe at the head. If you cannot manipulate it in this way, enlarge the hole slightly and use vitriol if necessary. And if there are more than one stones, push out the largest first near the bladder, then strike downwards, pull it out, and the smaller ones afterward if there are any more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 If it is very large, you must make a larger incision.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For the sick person, there are two things that happen: either he dies, or urine comes out repeatedly because the wounds cannot heal; but you must still try to drain it, or break it with pliers, as long as you can do so in pieces; and when you have finished your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and cover it with a damp cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and cold water and cold rosewater, to cool the abscess; then make the patient lie down on his neck, and do not undo the binding until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you undo it, immerse the place well in oil and water, then treat it with healing ointment of diaphanicum and basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 If abscesses and corrosions occur in the wound and the blood congeals in the bladder, and the urine is retained in this way so that it does not flow with the urine: then boil your foot in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, the bladder will rot and perforate; then clean the wound with water, oil, and linen, and help it in all possible ways until it heals; and it is necessary that every hour you treat it, you tie his legs together, and gather the medicines on the affected area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small and it is guided by a rod and thrust into, and urine cannot be released; cure it as I say next, you should cut it many times, except that you are excused from cutting due to this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already proved it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron foret in the form of this figure and pointed at four angles into one taper:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take thread and tie it around the rod under the stone so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then push the awl gently into the rod until it reaches the stone; and turn the awl little by little in the stone, as much as you can pierce the stone from another side; soon urine will come out, then press your hand on what is still held inside the stone that is within the rod.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is ever broken and jumps with urine, the patient recovers; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, put thread under the stone and another above, then insert a probe towards the stone between two veins, pull it out, release the sinew, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; treat it until it heals.
de la piere des femmes	from the female's stone (meaning ovarian cyst)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens rarely that a stone should be in a woman's womb, and if it ever happens, the cure is difficult, and it is forbidden for four reasons: the first is that by chance the woman may be a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well how to reveal herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 The third method is that by chance you cannot find a woman skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth method is that the woman's stone is deeper than a man's, so it requires a more profound incision, causing great fear. If such necessity arises, then you must take a skilled midwife, even if she is difficult to find, and if one cannot be found, do not hesitate to use a subtle cast; present a wise woman as bail or one who knows a part of the art, and command her to perform the incision of the stone. Ensure that the woman is a virgin; then she must push down with her fist or base and search for the stone; if she finds it, she should constrain it under her fist, and you must command her to push her fist or hand into the patient, and press her left hand firmly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If it is found, it must be moved slowly and steadily from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike on the stone in the root of the thigh near the middle of the bone where movement occurs, so that the stone can be felt in that part; and do not move your hand above or below the stone, and it should be cut off at the first small piece; then push the finger into the incision, if you feel the stone, enlarge the wound so that the stone can pass through easily, and know that there are many types of stones: for example, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 Recognize the signs to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 If the wound opens again, place broken vitriol on it and hold for an hour until the wound stops bleeding; then return to your work until the stone is expelled, and have instruments as I said for helping you extract the stone from men; and if the wound opens again, and it is an artery that has been cut, put powder on the place and bind with straps and bandages, do not start it again, leave the stone and do not draw it out, for there is a chance the patient may die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is abated and the wound heals, return to your work, and extract the stone when it protrudes.
de hernie carnouse	of a soft hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquouse is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white chyle, which is beneath the curd of the kidneys, containing the egg; and it is called "chyle", and sometimes it is properly in the egg's membrane, if one thinks that it is another egg; and it is the skin of the kidney between the white chyle that we have said; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this aquouse is due to weakness that comes from the kidneys, and this matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes there comes percussion on the head, and this moisture has many colors: either it declines to yellow, or without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more often; and these are signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white like we have said, it is a sign of abscesses, which grow long as the figure of an egg, and do not open the head, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the very cloth [linen], then it is considered an abscess with part of the egg; and since the moisture is between the skin and the white albumin, one can feel it well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, probe thoroughly for its form, which has been described before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the intrusion, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we cure with iron, the patient should be cleansed to our power and his body's fullness; then have him lie on his back, upon something a little raised, and put lots of cloths beneath him; then sit on his left side, and command the attendant to sit at the right, and stretch out the rod to one of the two ribs near the shoulder; then take the leech, and cut the skin between them with it along its length up to the joint, and your incision should be completely straight in dividing the skin as far as the white albumin; then carefully scrape off the subcutaneous fat according to your power; then pierce the albumin all around with a large needle, and draw out all the liquid, and then put your onions [tampons], and suture the albumin; do not touch the joint, but only the albumin; cut everything or in pieces carefully so that you do not return the liquid; if the egg bursts from your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the procedure for the abscess; then join the two leaves of the joint at a suture, then treat the wound as with other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to break the vessels that are susceptible to bleeding, doubting the flow of blood; then strike the coccyx at the entire suspension and extract the egg, and heal as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if an ulcer is assembled into two parts together, know that these are the branches; if you strike the other part as you have done the first equally, then draw out the blood, and put dampened linen in oil of roses in the wound; and put other dampened linen in wine and oil, and put them on both sides, and put cloths doubled over on top, and tie it all with a rope according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take the two cloths and use linen strips in this way and sew them together into a collar around the wound, and one of the heads takes hold of the base up to the back, and the other at the handle part; and the other two heads are on either side, and the rest should be drawn together at the knot of the bandage; and sometimes this branch of cautery is used in place of iron surgery, and it involves taking a sharp cauterizing tool, striking the skin of the wound, and heating it as we have said so that the white pus that contains the ulcer is exposed; then take the cautery in this shape, and pierce the pus with small holes, and scrape off the pus with this hot cauterizing tool:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And the blow in every manner that you can, as long as you are heating everything; and ensure that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more salveable; and be mindful of the management of blood, and mindful of the works of incision; and if anything happens contrary to this, or abscess chafing or bleeding or something else, then cure what happens contrary to this, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 If the patient is afraid and does not want to wait for this work because of its horribleness, then perform perforation, as I told you, and it is that when you are certain by the signs that we have mentioned that the aphrosis is present, then make the patient sit on a raised seat; then perforate the abscess in the area below entirely with a spatula wide, and place the perforation along the length of the body; let the holes be large so that all the pus can flow out; then put cotton over the area, hold it in place, and allow the remaining pus to drain out, then cure until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not prevent the pus from coming out of the opening of the wound, then you must insert a reed or the instrument used to treat the pus of dropsy, as its shape has been described earlier; and enlarge the hole in the wound, and know that the pus returns, and is collected after six months or so, and when it is collected as before, then the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess on the cheek
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the section of this remedy there is fear in many positions, so it seems that one should use more [of it]; and I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, many abscesses come from the body, and especially in the head; and this is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 This is about excessive sour and acute moisture spread to the joints or from impact; and the color of the abscess according to the body's color; it does not hurt, but is a serious abscess; and sometimes an abscess becomes swollen and hard, and of such a color, and occasionally comes from the artery or vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it comes from the artery, it can be recognized by the abscess's hot position when you press on it; and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 The patient who has swelling of the neck is known by his disposition at the expression of the touch of the fingers, and can well perform the incision on this appearance, and on other things; it is that you cut the cartilage of the throat, then is the egg in the head, and the yolk runs out white and clear, and delivers the suspensory from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the egg is already soft with these things born, then it is necessary that you draw out the egg and crush it; and if it is towards the white or in that which is within the vessels, it is necessary that you deliver all that tender part and crush it.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the birth of the hatchling is on its left side, you must break it completely and pull out the egg as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, apply the wound with damp wool in oil and wine, then heal it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess on the cheek
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess enclosed by a cover resembling a boil, with the softening of the throat, and the patient groans heavily as he goes; and the cure for this disease is in great danger as above, and yet we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 You must make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then you place the suspensory bandage below the knees at your elbows, around all the vessels near the penis, and tighten them with a master; then stretch them out fully; then cut through the foreskin sharply wide from the root of the penis, until they are exposed, and then flay it on each side as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples; then insert a double-threaded needle where the vein has appeared, and tie it to the first joint where the vision is present, and tie it directly to the other end; then pierce them evenly, according to the length of the body, and remove any corrupt tissues; then treat the wound as one would an arrow wound, so that no vessels leak the blood from the foreskin; because there is no harm in this, and if all the vessels have vision, you must draw the foreskin over all the vessels; so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dry out and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the sifac
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The occurrences of this condition are due to the section that opens or extends on the abdomen in the area of the inguinal region, as a result of which the intestines descend from that incision towards one of the kidneys; and this incision is either the opening or the extension of it, and these two types of conditions occur for various reasons: either by impact, or by jump, or by fall, or by lifting of heavy objects, and similar things; and the signs when it is the extension of the inguinal region, are that it happens little by little over a long period, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal up to the fully developed stage because the inguinal region follows the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the intestines, which brings on sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear differently, under the skin close by, and this is due to the discharge of the intestines and the body expelling the contents of the intestine.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines are expelled through the anus, and they are retained inside, causing great pain to the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, there is fear, for which it is necessary to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 And the method of work is that you instruct the patient to pull out the intestine with their hand inside through the wound if it can be reached; then hold their neck between your hands, and lift the thighs; then cut the skin over the kidneys longwise; then push fingers into the groin openings according to what is necessary for opening the wound, making sure that the testicles can come out; then remove the peritoneum that is below the skin of the kidneys, until the white peritoneum becomes exposed on all sides; then insert your index finger in the place where the kidney is, in the place that is between the white peritoneum that is below the skin of the abdomen and the second layer of peritoneum, and remove what is behind the abdomen and between the second layer of peritoneum; then move your hand to the right inside the kidney area, and move the white peritoneum up towards your left hand, and lift the abdomen towards the wound; instruct the assistant to stretch the abdomen upward, and untie what is in front behind the ligament; look for any intestine or hardened peritoneum with your fingers, and if you find anything, push it into the abdominal cavity; then take a large needle with thread made of ten threads, and insert it into the back part of the peritoneum, which is after the skin of the kidneys; after the abdomen, then sew the edges that appear from the threads, until there are four threads; then arrange them in the shape of a cross and sew the peritoneum, as we have said is below the skin of the kidneys, with a strong ligature of two parts; then wrap the edges of the threads, and sew them together with two parts, so that no servants who feed it can enter it, unless an infected cow comes to it; and tie again the ligature according to the first ligature length of two fingers of that one, and after these two ligatures leave a large space below the kidney area as before described; then sew in the rounded part where the abdomen is, then sew in the part below the skin of the kidneys until it becomes smooth and rounded, as we have said earlier; then apply oil-soaked linen to the wounds, and apply the ligature that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes white boils are cauterized as we have said, after incision, due to fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 For this often happens and leave the ligament until it shrinks by itself; and if it delays in falling off, you should soak with hot water and place on it what has been said, until it falls off; then treat the wound with another remedy, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a soft hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy, I have never seen anyone who dared to make a cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is made like a graft which is attached to the bone, in this manner you tie the veins, above the wound lightly on the underside; then cut in the middle and treat the abscess from those who are working on it, until the veins fall off; and treat it as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 Sometimes comes gangrene in the anus, as we have said, and do not touch any of the intestines to the wound; if some are touched, it is a mistake, and repair every hour; and still if it stays too long in this place, the wound or pus forms, until the intestines come out; and this happens by the spreading of pus which is in the anus, as we have said, because it spreads, then it becomes softened and inflamed the anus and opens; and it is treated by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: the patient lies on their back between your hands, then cut the swollen anus open widely according to the size of 3 fingers; and then extract the pus which is below the skin that surrounds it, then take the lancet and place it on the visible pus area; and press fully on the stomach, then sew the two visible areas of the pus on top of the tip of the lancet, and sew one and the other; then extract the tip of the lancet, but do not cover or stretch the wound or anything else, as I told you in the treatment of the graft of the intestines; then treat it by the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cauterize the hairs (or veins), if it becomes inflamed and cures the wound, do so until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sutures are confined and have no appearance in the wound, and cauterizations are more appropriate here and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin around the eyes
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin around the eyes is softened in some men, because the charms inside are softened and there is a discharge to be seen; and it is necessary, when it is seen that it needs to be cured, to make the patient lie on his back, and to strike the softened skin on the natural skin; then to bring together the two lips at a stitch, and if you see, sew first the excess of the softened skin with 3 or 4 stitches firmly; then to strike between the stitches, and let the cure as for other wounds, until it is healed, and bind the thread.
dou chastrement	of the pounding
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 I mention here that castration is discussed in our law, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary for only two reasons: the first is that animals respond when asked about castration and their cure; and the second, because we often need castration of certain animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, pigs, and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 Therefore, castration is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the method of castration by attraction, we seat the animal in warm water until the genitals are softened and relaxed; then we grab them with our hand, holding them until they remain and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 For the branding of the cattle: you must dye the beast, then press the hide of the testicles with your left hand, tie the suspensory, and strike each one with a hot iron where you have well scorched it; leave any small spot unscorched and the subtle scourge that is on the vassels; and this kind of branding is more effective than the one made by attraction, because by attraction, something from the testicles may remain accidentally, which makes the beast desire lust; then heal the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodite
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 Hermaphroditism is according to two manners in humans: one is that between the two testicles remains open as the figure of a woman's genitalia according to the nature, where it has hair, and sometimes in court they pass urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other method is in women, and it has above the thumbnail as thick as a rod and they prick.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment of men and women is that you cut all the hemorrhoids together, and treat them as other wounds; in the second method, for men whose urine jumps through the skin of the scrotum, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	Of the tentergen (or tending)
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 Tumor (Tentigene) is a hemorrhoid on the natural part that is too unsightly to see; and some women have it as big as a hand, and this is treated.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 It is necessary that you color the superfluity of the tumor (Tentigene) with your hand or onions, and cut it lightly; do not go too deep, so that blood does not flow out, then treat it with other treatments until it becomes healed; and for another hemorrhoid that comes from the mouth of the vagina, and pus flows out, and resembles a cow, therefore they called it "disease cow" by the ancients.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 It is necessary to cut it (the shoulder), as we have said previously, and to care for it until it heals.
de erratique	Of the hernia (or protrusion)
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 The hernia is one of three types: when the nature of the woman is not perceived or the opening is small; it is natural by birth or accidental due to disease; or it is caused by hard or subtle pressure, and is made complete in the womb, in the flanks, or in the lower abdomen, wherever it may be; and it should be distinguished from conceiving, childbirth, and from flowers developing; and its recognition is through the examination of the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the swelling appears near the hand or the armpit.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 If it is a subtle case and the patient is near death, hurry up and proceed like this: put your two fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread apart; then form the two shoulders round when the subtle case is hard, and be careful about the discharge; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the shoulder, and make the woman lie still every day so that it does not heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the case is hard and large, you must cut it with a flat instrument resembling the leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the discharge is of watery nature, suspend it on an onion and cut; have the medicines ready that are strengthening blood, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with many eggs; then bring a large bandage, so that the wound does not heal; and in this way let it be long and provide a dry linen tent; then cure other diseases until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when a child is born in marriage, it should be covered according to this manner, unless the birth is an abscess enlarged.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For at the abscess enlarged in marriage, one should not make any attempt to treat it with fire.
des emorroides	If the nature of a woman is not perceived or it is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental due to disease that comes about; or it is by false conception, or due to subtle or thick sperm, and it is fully formed in the anus, or in the side, or under the ribs, or wherever it may be; and they cannot conceive, give birth, or bring forth flowers; and knowledge of this is by the observation of the belly. If the efflux of blood is nearby, whether at your hand or at your right side. If it is subtle sperm, and it is nearby the two leeks (testicles), hurry and proceed thus: put your two hands together, and the woman should be on her back, with her legs spread; then form the two leeks, until the subtle sperm is ripe, and the efflux of blood stops. Then take wool, wet it in oil, and place it over the area. Let the woman lie down on her back each day so that it cannot heal. And if the sperm is hard and thick, it should be cut with a spatula shaped like the leaf of myrtle. If the efflux is of false conception, let it stop at the cervix and cut it; and have medicines to stop bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, together with much egg white. Then prepare a large reed-like straw, so that the wound cannot heal; and in this way it should be kept long, and prepare a tent of dry linen; then cure as necessary until it is healed. And when false conception comes in marriage, it should be covered in this manner, unless the abscess has become hardened. For an abscessed area that has become hardened in marriage, one should not try to heal it.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without care commonly occur, and when hemorrhoids become old they become inflamed; and we have said in the division the similarities, signs, and I will say here those that receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and inflammations, when they are completely in marriage and do not appear to sensation, should not be cured by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those that are at the mouth of the vagina, one can feel them, these are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold house, then set the instrument for tweezers, and place it on its roots, then sprinkle medicinal powders that restrict blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood powder and incense, and similar things; then press her feet to the wall for an hour, then immerse her in a cold bath; and if blood flow comes, make her sit in a decoction of sumac bark, apple tree bark, ivy and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make a poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 If it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If it does not, make her wear mustard plasters on the back and around the breasts without wounding them; then take flax, wet it in juice of plantain or elder with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess settles down, treat the wound with ointment until it heals; and that which is called "albathir" is red, resembling a rough crust, if necessary cover it as I have said in the previous text; and then continue to heal it until it is well.
des apostemes de la marris	3. When abscesses in the anus are treated...
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many kinds of abscess come in marriage, such as carbuncles and painful abscesses, herpes, scabs, festering ulcers, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.
