Therefore, I must explain in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in marriage, which is not like those that stick to the bowels; and if you wish to know about ironwork, see if the abscess is acute at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Then do not hurry to pierce, but let it heal as the pain subsides; and then make the patient sit on a chair, or two small chairs where he leans, and support his back and assemble his feet at the parts away from the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a strong rope; then bring the key towards the right side, and lead in the instrument used to open the bladder, so that the form follows; it is necessary that when you see the instrument brought in, you poke the right first to know the depth of the bladder, so that nothing inside comes out more deeply than it should, and does not hurt the patient; if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the bladder with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt it; and it must place the horn of the instrument above, and mark the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess is opened and it is treated by hand, you should cover it with lard oil; and when the boil is empty, you must put moistened linen in oil rose or green dry oil into the wound; place the linen bandage from the wound to the full length of the arm, and place it on top of the arm and over the clean linen bandage soaked with vinegar or honey; then treat it for two days after that with ointment until it is healed; and sometimes lift the arm and the wound with vinegar and honey enema, and then with vinegar or roots of lilies and aristolochia longa boiled; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is healed in the marrow, you must be careful not to burn with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 Firstly, the woman must recognize the shape of natural childbirth and its signs when she is close to giving birth, and desires to urinate: then hasten the infant to be born; afterward, know that this delivery is according to natural shape, and the child exits with his head, followed by the placenta; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her abdomen, so that the infant comes quickly; for when it moves towards the head, the placenta follows, and the membranes are expelled from their waste products through good purification; and that which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 It sometimes happens that one falls on one's feet, the body or shoulders, hands, or belly, and it happens to turn by chance around the neck, and in other bad ways; therefore, it is necessary for the bailiff to be wise and skilled in these matters, and to avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the figures on how to help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out naturally from its head and the woman gives birth loudly, and her strength is weak, make her sit on a saddle or have other women hold her; anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then insert the baile between her fingers using the little spatula as shown below:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 And split the second bone, and strike its nail where the moisture that is within is driven out; and hold the woman's belly until the baby comes out, and if it does not come out, you must cleanse the woman with musk of fenugreek with camomile oil; then make her take and vomit from condisi, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: now the baby will be born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands come out, you must carefully set them back in place bit by bit; and if they cannot be put back, place the woman on the stool, and lift her feet up high; then tilt the stool onto the ground, and tie the woman so she does not shake with it; and if the hands still cannot be put back and the child is dead, cut the hands with the knife that is placed here before, extract the child, and set them back in place as well.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 from the issue of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes out on its feet, you must lift it up; then turn it bit by bit until it is even; then take one of the feet and stretch it bit by bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 It may jump up to the hinges, if commanded to strike, and make it vomit with convulsions; if it jumps away, let it be as God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, then turn it slowly, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	And then turn it gently.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if it does not come out as we have said, then take the mussel from a high place, oil of sesame, and softened gum, and grind all in a mortar; put this ointment inside her, and turn her upside down; and when she is softened below, apply the collyrium of myrrh, and put it under, and leave it for an hour; then have her sit on the chair, then make her vomit and hold her mouth and nose, and press lightly on her stomach because the infant jumps now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the birth of the child on its thighs
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this form, place the belly's edge on his hands, palm to palm; then lay him on his back and let his feet hang down, and he should be lying on the bed; bend your hands, palm to palm, and then take hold of his hands above his stomach, and break the hips bones beneath until it is prepared below; if the child does not leap, grasp its feet and move them forward, then move its stomach upwards, then place your hands; rock the child gently from side to side; and command the woman to catch the child as soon as it comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	the child coming out with a wide hand stretch.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to devise a way to return the hand: if you cannot return it, raise the woman and walk; if she cannot walk, make her sit on the bed, spread her legs widely apart; then bring the mustard plaster that I have mentioned earlier; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the chair, and try to return the hand naturally; and deliver the child according to its natural shape, and make her vomit, and command her to catch the child as soon as it comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Hold the baby by its neck, spread your hands wide, and turn your face toward the mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 You must have the servant grip his hand, then twist it little by little and gently; and when it is equalized, you put above it the muscle-healing balm of alum and oil, as we have said, then you command that it move little by little; and when you have done this, make him sit on the seat, and command him to take hold of it; and make him vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same way, treat the second one as well.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When the afterbirth comes in this way entirely, you strike the afterbirth with your nail until it is voided; and if the child presses on its face and neck, you strike from below so that it is not held, and the child dies; then push the child down, as needed, and command the woman to take hold of it lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	From the birth of twins,   (Note: In medieval medicine, "twins" was used to refer to any kind of duality or pairing, not necessarily two human babies.)
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born frequently, and sometimes three or four; and this is not strange, and it often happens.   (Note: This text uses the medieval counting system where Roman numerals are used for numbers greater than one.)
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 Two are strange things that do not live, unless they are named; I know what they are, as they are multiplied, and are sought by the one who devises them, who is linked to filth; and sometimes they arise naturally like all undergrowth, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 If they arise forcefully, then the cure is as we have said, and let it be handled by a skilled person, and do promptly and lightly whatever it does; and do in such a way that it moves towards healing.
de plusors enfans	Of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the womb in the first month or second month or third month or fourth month or fifth month, or up to the fifteenth, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of a sage man; and it is necessary that the skilled person knows this, for by chance similar things may happen; do accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	Of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you cure a woman of a dead child or an unborn child, as I said in the division, and it does not come out naturally, and you are forced to work by hand; then you must know if the woman is of good virtue and has no accident or fear of death; the woman should lie on her back with her hips inclined downwards and legs raised; and the minister should hold her thighs in two parts, or tie her to the bed so she is not treated from below the child; then anoint the mouth of the mother with moist oils mixed with musk and fennel seed and linseed; then oil the hands of the minister with these oils and these musks; then gently insert them into the mother, then seek where the membranes are located that can be reached, and make sure the fetus is exposed at its head; then pierce the membranes in her womb or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or in the vagina or near the sides, and if the piercing is on the feet, pierce or poke them and press on the middle ribs; and the minister must hold the membrane with his right hand, and place the thumb between his left-hand fingers, and gently push it anywhere where we have said, until it reaches an empty state; and this is the shape of the membrane:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 Then pierce towards the other joint, or the one you need to use for extraction, so that the dislocations are even; and then align it equally by moving from one side to another, causing movement to occur, and keep the joints closed for movement, as shown in the figure:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 If there remains a part of it, then press some oil from his fingers onto that part and push it into the remaining part; and if there is no part left, then place the joint where it belongs or higher up, and do this until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be returned due to the tightness, you must wrap it up in a cloth until it slips out; then crush it at the joint of the foot or near the bone, and do this with both hands and feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's head is large and it is narrow in the birth canal, or it has a pointed crown assembled, you must push the spiked spatumile between your hands, and break the crown and extract the water; or you can use the instrument called "almidach", from which the shape of the instruments or chapter that follows this comes; and do the same with the child if it comes out naturally with a large head; then pull the bones apart with the pliers, and if the child jumps out and is held back by force, it should be cut, as far as the moisture that is in the wrong place goes; and if it cannot come out, you should hit it into pieces where you can. And if it swells in the abdomen or under the ribs, you must pierce it until the moisture escapes.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on its feet, the drawing out is light, and the correction towards the mouth of the bladder is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is protruding from the abdomen or the anus, then you must pull it back covered by a cloth over the hand; and pressing the abdomen or the anus, straighten it out until the moisture that is there corrects; and if other members are dislocated, and the head remains, push the thumb into the anus deeply and draw it out to the mouth of the anus; then insert a finger or two, and pull it further; and if the mouth of the anus is narrowed due to abscess heat that has come, you should not strain it, instead you should administer moist and fat substances; and you should administer plasters, and apply them in warm softening and moistening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the baby is on its side and you can make it straight, apply what we have said in our treatment for live births; and if this cannot be done, tear it apart piece by piece and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And when this is done, apply what we have said in treating abscesses that come during marriage; and if bleeding occurs, it should be put under strict restraint, and other treatments should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman in whom an infant had died in the womb, then consulted another on this matter, and brought it back to life.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time an abscess came in the armpit, and swelled so much that it burst, and began to putrefy.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the treatment, and I thought for a long time, but could not stop the wound from bleeding.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong dressing, and out came a bone, then after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I wish to treat the wound and remove many bones as long as the woman is in a good position; and she should remain in this condition for a long time and then after a little while a little bit of pus will come out; and I have not remembered this chapter being used except when masters find something strange which they know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the wife to her place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the translation for the next sentence:
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 The horns should be more subtle than the restraining instrument, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the rod should be wide, and the edges of the branches should be, and a half palm in length; and between the two limbs should be two similar rods, which are closed on both ends, half a palm long or a little more; and these two rods are inserted into the wife's mouth to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another form, more subtle and lighter, should be made of a rod of ebony or boxwood in the likeness of pliers; and to each shoulder there should be two rods, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the wife with the entire instrument, make her sit on the bed, her feet hanging and legs open, then insert the two rods together into the wife, and hold the head of the instrument under her thighs; then operate your hand with the whole instrument as you have done with pliers, according to the quantity that you wish to open the mouth of the wife, until he makes what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all covered and multiplied in their likenesses; and when the masters have arranged them, the work is more urgent, and higher for humans due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not uncover the instrument unless you have arranged it, as their necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to retain her afterbirth, then make her vomit with emetics, and hold your hands at her mouth and anus; if she jumps due to this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If not, take the spoon and make the syrup or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the dead person, such as rue, anise, camomile, cassia, centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked in water over fire; then put a cord or syringe filled with the liquid into the mouth of the dead person, and hold it until the vapors enter the body of the dead person; then make the dead person vomit as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The second sentence to translate:
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if the dislocation remains after this cure and does not heal as instructed, command the patient to wet her left hand in sesame oil or musk oil, then put it on nature, and seek again; when she has found it, take it and stretch it little by little straight, so that the muscles do not resist at extraction; but it should be moved gently to the right and to the left, and then pull; it will come and release.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 If the mouth of the anus has been stretched out (rectum), we have said the cure is to empty and fumigate with herbs; if it does not heal as we have said, ensure you do not pull too hard; but it is necessary that he who is at the mouth of the anus, bind him to the woman's leg, then cleanse with ointment four-medicine; when he can be pulled and reset, it will heal again; however, if he comes out badly, there will be a bad smell in the stomach and head, and it will hurt the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore it is necessary that appropriate fumigations are provided for this case: no ancient has proven the fumigation of parsley and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain the flowers and seconding (afterbirth) is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it resembles glass like a dog's head, and the head is placed in its nature, with wide shoulders over the fire; and let there be fumigation over the coals, and the tinder until it is burned out, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born without a proper foundation, but it has been blocked by some subtle obstruction; therefore, it is necessary to pierce the obstruction at its appropriate place, not with a sharp spatula, and be careful that it does not touch the wound; then put damp linen soaked in wine and oil on it, and treat with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will stay reset, put or insert a splint of wood, and leave it for several days, and let it be removed when the bones appear to have moved in rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes comes this sudden swelling of wound or abscess; it is necessary to cover the sore: if healed, as we have said with a splint of wood.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula at its foundation   (In this context, a fistula is an abnormal passageway or channel between two organs or parts of the body.)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodules, and those that come out from above the foundation swell, or in the space of two parts, there may be one fistula or more; and when this nodule is old, it opens up, and moisture awakens blistering or a subtle boil, and sometimes these fistulas become persistently draining; and they are recognized by those who are experienced that it has either discharge or ventosity when the patient experiences discharge, and in some cases, it gushes outward.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate to the bladder, and halfway down the penis; they reach up to the knee joint, and up to the calf of the leg.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus one recognizes the fistula persistent at its base, and not persistently; it is that you bite your thumb or base of the finger, and bite a thin awl of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 If there is twisting, then insert a thin splint or horsehair, feeling the splint or hair at your thumb; and if you do not feel it, and no pus, gas, wind, or worm comes out as we have said: know that it will not pierce; hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is open to the bladder or conducts urine, if it leaks urine and cannot be sealed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it is pierced up to the knee joint, then the splint comes up to its place; if there is no twisting and the pain disappears around it, it is that it should be bound there, and no medicine or ointment helps it; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure but labor and the vain efforts of foolish healers who interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In a person who is not a Persian and not old, for the hope of health through fire, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lifts the legs up to the thighs, and has the thighs inclined towards the abdomen; then push a tent of pitch or plank, if there is curvature, until you know where the dislocation comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels it around the base, then you must push your index finger there, until you feel that the dislocation has been pierced; and if it is discovered where the dislocation is, either the bone or the flesh, then know that it is a Persian one; do not touch it further as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 One should say that some can be healed well, but this happens seldom; and the aid given, it is this: one should heat the fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as mentioned before; and push it all hot into the fistula, until it comes out from the base; and do this twice or three times, until you know that these charred parts are burned, which resemble a feather of an eye; and then cure with moistened bandages in butter, until those charred parts disappear, then cure with soothing ointment.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If it cannot be healed otherwise and if the fistula is not opened up to its base, put a thick covering of skin or linen between your thumb and the fistula; so that you can see the fistula through this thin covering; then press from the beginning of the fistula and push it towards the fistula, then the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the end of the fistula; and the bladder will be released, with the char remaining; then burn off those charred parts that resemble a feather of an eye, and leave none behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the flesh is soft and cuts between you and the abscess, cauterize it with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 The fire cautery brings two good things: burning of these joints joined together and stopping the flow of blood and removal of moisture; then treat wounds soaked in soft cheese or broth crushed chaff, until the limbs are hardened, and the charred joints are placed in the chaff; then treat the wound with ointments hard as stone and dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it will be healed and will not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	If a fistula arises until it reaches the full depth and is located outside of the body, you should press on the affected area or foundation, and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the wound, and between it is fabric or hide or bone that is about to pierce, there should be no more than one way of faith and hope through the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize as we have said, or you hit to the bottom, or if boils, treat as previously; but do not go too deep so that you do not cover the foundation holding it, and the pus comes out voluntarily; then treat, as we have said; by chance, it may heal, or remove that covering and clean when it is pierced from the foundation, either through fabric or other instrument appointed; then remove the dead flesh that is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part distant from the foundation: this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: when you insert the probe into the fistula and it is at the base of the skin above, take a sharp probe according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	Then push one threaded needle into two, and push the tent all along the thread into the fistula up to the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 When the fistula is at the margin of the base within, then pull out the thread of that probe so that you can insert your finger or base; and pull out its head and bring the two ends together, holding one against the other, and leave them for a day or two; and squeeze it occasionally, until the threads break the charred parts between them, and they close; then heal the wound until it is healed and clean.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, make it open in all ways that you can, unless it is too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is not advisable to cover a dislocated joint with a plaster, and then cure it while it is still swollen, as we have said, until it heals.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The form of the sharp probe for making a fistula is very pointed at one end and beveled on the other, so that it does not harm what should not be harmed, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Emerodies occur in two ways: either they are within the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are both small and large ones; and on the surface, there is already blood, and there is one or more, and they are displaced from the foundation and from the head of the foundation; but those that are displaced have a little moisture, and at the same time or a little citron juice or blood, and have the color of the body; and the treatment for those that have them within the foundation is to command the patient to strain by urinating in chambers until the foundations loosen, and this will be noticed by the children; if you hurry, and place it in tongs, or hold it with your nail, then strike at its roots; and if the hook cannot hold it due to moisture, take it with cloth or cotton, or a piece of camel's hair; and stretch them out on your hands, then strike, and sprinkle some hot powders on top that are in place of cautery; or cauterize them as said in the chapter of cautery, then treat them with other cures until they are healthy; and if the foundations cannot loosen, clisterize the patient with biting and sharp clisterium to clean what is at the foundation, so that it can come out openly; when the patient feels this, and the filaments have left the foundation, the cure is easy; and it is necessary to take them with your nail or tongs, strike them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healthy, and fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 You must apply the stitching in this manner: take a twisted thread and insert it into a needle, then draw the thread above and pierce the needle from another side, and turn both ends of the thread below the needle and make it large; bind the thread, then knot it, and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, leaving the superfluity of blood; then place a moistened cloth in rose oil or wax on the foundation and place it on top, and command the patient to rest; then leave it until it seeps, and when it is drained, cure it with ointment and other treatments until it heals.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	The drying of wounds or foundations.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often, the drying out of wounds occurs in the intestines due to natural constraints and when the disease is old and medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is necessary that you cut the bark of a willow twig or your fingernail above, so it does not get wet; then heal it until it is dry as needed; and if it cannot heal, repeat the shaving stronger than before, as much as it bleeds, and be peeled; then heal it until it is healed.
dou fremit	The trembling (or shivering)
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 A boil is a small growth occurring near the body and it grows greatly; and sometimes the frost bites it, and it feels as cold as death, and spreads throughout the whole body, and more in hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the cure is that you take a cane of an owl feather or a strong eagle feather and place the cane on the frostbite so that it circles around the frostbite entirely; then turn your hand all along the cane until you catch the frostbite completely, and immerse it fully, and peel the frostbite of its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see it (like a chain of iron or steel), do this according to the following form, and be subtle inside and pull it out from above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce (the swelling), but hold it tightly and press it; and if you see it (the swelling), cauterize it as described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a plaster   \* The text describes how to make a plaster for treating wounds or swellings.\* This sentence is describing the shape that the plaster should have, specifically "the form of a plaster."\* In medieval medical texts, the term "clistere" often refers to a type of ointment or salve used in wound treatment.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At times they make a silver or arsenic enema, or molten lead or mercury; and at times they make of these instruments small and large, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, when administering the treatment for children and the weak and sickly, the instruments are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the enema is large or small; it is tied in this manner above, according to this method:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 And it should have an opening where the belly is connected, as you see, and the shoulders inside pierced; and on one side there should be two holes, and on the other one; and the belly or arm should be filled with medicine from a beast's bladder or parchment, and pierced all around with small holes, and there should be space between each hole, then thread a strong cord through these holes in X or around, and sew up the belly as if it were a bag; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong cord, then clisterize; and this is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clistere with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the ministers hold it with their two hands together, until it is completely visible, then pull out the clistere, and tie the patient's legs to the floor so that the medicine comes out when needed; if it remains for a whole night, it is more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you want to treat a disease of abdominal distention, and the medicine works quickly, repeat it until it becomes healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if the hemorrhoids are either founded or abscessed, it should be cleansed in the same way as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle enema where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the previous section the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the care for hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are by means of a stone, the cutting of swords and knives, or lances or fists or arrows, or similar things; or those that are made according to the laws of the body, such as wounds on the neck, head, chest, abdomen, liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with the simple wounds of the head, because remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound or sore comes, and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is from an arrow piercing or similar things, and the skin is torn completely and the wound is large; doubt the formation of an abscess: let it drain immediately of its own head if blood comes from the wound, and let it heal on the contrary of the injured part; and empty the patient's repletion with wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it does not drain, let its meat be reduced, and do not drink wine, nor eat meat; and put on the wound, if an abscess forms there, only soft cotton soaked in rose oil or vinegar steeped; and if there is no abscess, put on the wound if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, a little of the following powder: and if the fire has moved it, put some ointments on until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like the size of a sword and of similar appearance, and the lips cannot be brought together by pressing, then join them with stitches, as I will explain for abdominal wounds, through stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed by bone, gapes, and does not hold firm, cover it; then heal the wound with medicine, put hard flesh instead of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick foods such as cooked heads (testes) and wheat, also things like cabbages and similar items.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find or skin corruption that is not connected to the bone, cover it all and throw it away, then heal it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein which cannot be stopped by medicines, you should try to stop the artery; and if you find the artery dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if that does not help, cauterize (it).
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if the wounds are small and simple, it is an easy cure: and it is that you put this powder which cements them once the herb has moved (it).
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the method of the powder is: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of live coal, and grind it finely, then apply it to the wound, press it firmly, until it exudes well and joins all its blood; then bind it well, and leave it to heal, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	Sometimes this is done only with chalk, when no incense or dragon's blood is available, but the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the fire has burnt the wound, in that case do not put this powder on it; but apply some digestive ointments or barley flour made with water and honey until it boils; then heal it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with subtle forceps; and I will tell you afterwards about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	Of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes in or on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between that and one on the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is nerves, there should be no other device except to let it heal naturally and not put anything restricting, because this harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, as the nature of nerves is cold, and their continuation with the brain which is the highest member; but be the medicine soft, such as boiled water in sweet oil, and apply warm water to it in the same manner, and other suitable remedies according to this method, and moist immediately.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, wrap it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and the flesh is swollen and full of pus, pierce it or lower its position; and if the arteries are cut, and blood flow ensues, stop it, lance it, and cauterize if necessary; and if the spines of the throat are cut or the veins, keep them closed, so that the flesh passes, if the vein rises on the throat chain and does not touch the throat but is returned according to its natural figure; then press gently, leave it for some days, then treat with rejected ointments until it heals; and if the wound has pressed against the bone, pierce it; and if there are pieces of bone, pull them out completely as you can, and those that you cannot have, leave until the wound festers, and make the issue drain and align it; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle powder on it as I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound caused by lance or knife.   --> of the lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a spear or knife wound and the wound is deep, check if the patient is showing signs of air escaping from the wound: know that the wound is fatal; and if it is not deep and the wound is fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder at first hour or bind it because the blood may dissolve the wound completely, return to the heart, and kill the patient; instead, apply attracting ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound for drainage of moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound 3 or 4 days, or more; no spasm or bad heart tremor caused by fear should appear; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Treat the wound and other treatments as long as it is healthy; but if it cannot heal, then know that there is a fistula; treat it accordingly.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 If the wound is a sword or knife incision, simple, deep or on the back, then treat what is in front of it; if it is large, sew it up; and if it is small, use powder, and if it is pressed against the bone, and has pieces of flesh, treat the wound and pull out the debris, unless they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound heal naturally, and apply extracts for other wounds as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	the dislocation of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The dismemberments of the abdomen are large, medium and small; from a large wound, any intestines occasionally protrude once, or the layers of the intestines, due to which their introduction [into the body] is difficult; and the stitching is more troublesome, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because they insert more intestines into it if not done carefully from inside out; because the intestines inflate suddenly when they feel cold, so they protrude more, and therefore a medium-sized wound is better, because one can reset the intestines to their place better than with others. And know that the abdominal incision is according to four types: the two common stitches occur in the abdominal incision, and the stitching of other wounds on the body and two other specific ones are common for other wounds; however, they are more proper with the abdominal incision, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestines protrudes from it, it is easy to set, as one of the two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm it in one of these ways: either moisten a sponge or dip a cloth only in tepid water, or cook it in tepid squill and cyperus and spike, and rub the intestines until the swelling disappears; and sometimes make wine-restrengnant, and warm it to help reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling separate, if you anoint the intestine with water or alum and malves cooked, for this way is closed the entrance to little; and if it cannot enter, then make a small opening in the wound with the instrument of which one copes hemorrhoids; and the first cure is warm it that it festers, but not too much that you should cut it without great necessity; and this is the instrument for slicing: slit it along the curve and do not spread it, and look at its shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines fall out, put it back in place according to its natural form in its proper location, if you have the power, for this is beneficial.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is in the part beneath the abdomen, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; if it is in the part beneath the abdomen, then raise the head and the hips higher than the parts beneath; and thus, when the hernia of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, direct your attention to making the injured part higher than the other. And so, direct this advice to large and small wounds alike.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 Place small wounds with what you have prepared, then take a compassionate person who will press the entire wound with his hand and bring the edges together; this is the common method of stitching, and it is that you take a needle or more than one, according to the size of the wound; leave some space from the edge of the wound and insert a needle with a strong thread; pierce the two layers of skin with the two layers of fat beneath, which is under the skin, until you pierce through this part; assemble the two edges of the fat together three times; then wrap a double thread around the needle in two places, then bring together the edges of the wound again, and leave some space, and insert another needle; tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue doing this until the entire wound is held together; the needles should be medium sized, neither too fine nor too thick, for very thin needles pierce through all the flesh, and very thick ones cannot enter well; do not push the needles too far from the flesh and skin, so they don't open or injure the wound before it heals; then tie the needle heads, so they don't hurt the patient while sleeping, and wrap cloth or bandages around the needle heads to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound heals; this method of stitching with needles is more useful for small wounds, because a single needle or two can perform the second stitch, and it is that you assemble the two layers of skin and the two layers of fat together with one needle where there is a strong thread; and when you have sewn all parts together, remove the needle to the part where you began, in the way cloth is rolled; leave space between each stitch the thickness of a small eggshell; this method of stitching is known as "the man's," and I sewed a wound with a man who had a belly, which was stabbed by a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, and the intestines were about two palms wide, and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I brought back the intestine when it had been twenty-four hours gone, and the wound healed up for fifteen days, and it was healed, and became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 They had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not heal him with any ointment, because I was in the place where none were found, nor any medicines; and I put cotton old twice a day on the wound, and washed it with water of honey until it became healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 Now I shall tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and thrust it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced the skin straight through, place the head of the thread or stitch where you have put in the needle, and pierce it again from the inside to the outside in the same manner; and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew as the tailor does fur, leaving a hole once on one side, and taking it up again on the other, until the stitching is completely done.
