Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second method of suturing, which Galen calls specifically, is as follows: one joins together the two parts naturally and applies the head of the needle to the other head, in this manner: stick a needle or head of the awl at one place, and pierce only that spot, leaving the two heads of the awl; then turn the needle and pierce from the outer part towards the inner part, through the two heads of the awl; then pierce both from the outer part towards the inner part, in the other two heads of the awl located on the opposite side; and this is the turned method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galiens uses this term and is confirmed by many, that one should sew the belly with two needles, each with thread in it; one needle should be pushed from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew corsets; know that when the wound is within the belly, the stitching is more painful than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgement of the wound is like that of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound full of blood, before the herbs have moved it, you should replace the intestines and the fat; then put powder healing char on it, and if the herbs have moved it, apply any ointment available until the wound closes; sew together each thread, and bind the sifac (?), and the mirror; then treat the wound as other wounds, until it heals; and if you don't have medicine, apply old cotton on it, as soon as it starts to close, and move it two times a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 You need no other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound communicates with the principal members, then you must moisten light linen with warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the edges, and under the buttocks; and if there is pain or pus in the belly, and this happens frequently, then you should clisterize with black wine, and the same applies if the pus comes up to the intestines; and pierce it through, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is perforated, and this is due to the inflammation of veins within it, and the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the hernia pops out of the wound, put it back in the same way as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned black, you must cut away the black part so that no blood comes from it, because there are veins and arteries there; then seize what is between the hernia sac, and hang the two heads hanging from the part below the wound to straighten the extraction when the hernia pops out, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the eyeball
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, because I have seen a man who was pierced or stabbed by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and there was discharge and flatulence; I cured it according to what I knew, and did not stop until it was healed, and the wounds closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it sew [the wound], I doubted that the patient had ill in his stomach; and he had no ill, but improved in better condition, and ate and drank; and said any experienced one that when it has a small wound in the intestine, that it should be tied up in such a way: take strong pincers, then gather the edges of the wound, and when the pincers have opened the mouth, place it on the two edges, so that it stretches its mouth open; and then strike the head, and keep it so that it cannot separate, then put another pincers after in the same way as before, until the wound is all taken up; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 If the head (of an organ) becomes inflamed in the intestine and brings no harm to the patient, it can be sewn up with a thin thread made from the intestine of an animal, like this: take a piece of that thread of intestine that is fairly sharp, then attach it to the head of the thread with a thin thread of flax, twist them together, then insert the thread into the needle and sew the intestine in this manner; and this method of stitching is not useful unless it follows the path of faith and hope. If the wound is large and wide, particularly if it is in one of the greater intestines, there is no trick or cure, except by subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	from fistula or that it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it heals and becomes swollen, is universally called "fistula", and the same when it breaks open and bows out.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And fistula is by truth a knot formed hard and white, where no pain is felt, and it swells in the same way as the feather of a bird; sometimes it clears up with a clear discharge, and other times thickens; sometimes shallow, and other times quite deep; I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, this is otherwise but by one of the nine causes: namely, by the smallness of blood or body; or by its corruption; or because there is hard flesh within, and above the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow; or it has too much pus; or the limb is paralyzed, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or corruption is a form of pestilence; or because the property in the region is slow digestion, and slow healing, and sluggish by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the medicines for treatment in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I will tell you how to treat a fistula that is made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistula occurs in all the members of the body; because there are fistulas that come from the great veins, arteries, nerves, or the intestine, bladder, kidneys, any of the ribs, spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and it is such that comes to the property of the main member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all the fistulas of this kind are difficult to cure, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if any fistula does not come up to the level that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it recognized, take a tent made of bee wax or iron, if the fistula is straight, pierce it; and if the fistula is twisted, search for a thin tent of wood, because the woods bend around the curvature; and if the fistula has been broken and you cannot find it with tents, cleanse it through one of the openings, because moisture runs from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then pierce it as skillfully as possible, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and if it is fully closed, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when pressed by your hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly understand the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or in any of the places that I have mentioned, then cut as described, and remove the rotten tissue and corrupt matter that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply situated directly, then you must cut through it completely, as much as possible, then place moistened tents filled with medicine in it, and push them to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluous matter that remains inside; and then apply fresh charmed oil, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is rotten from the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If a vein or nerve does not weigh down or the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is decay and blackness, remove all decay until it is entirely removed, then cure with charms for healing things until it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, make an incision as before, know that you are not going to the font: uncover and dig down until you reach the bottom, remove all decay, then restore the joint; and if it is thus healthy, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If the corruption is too deep, you cannot reach it; and if there is only a small rotten bone, and you can extract it with pliers, remove it with an instrument suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, remove them all without leaving any; and if moisture opposes you and there is no error or fear, use hammer, moisture, and fire, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove [the foreign body] within an hour, put something irritating on the wound around the bones, and leave it until the flesh is rotten all around the bone; and then the bones will be easier to remove. If it is a large bone, such as the leg or thigh, press only on the corruption until all the blackness is removed, then close the wound again. If there is a large part that has become corrupted and has reached the bone molecule, you should excise and cover everything up to the corruption, and then heal it until it heals; I will tell you of a fistula that happened in a man's leg, so take example and help from this.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 The young man was about thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within his body, so that the matter came to his leg, and he burst open with a large abscess, and had no reason to defecate; but they mistook it for folly and opened up the abscesses many times, and much matter came out, and it became a fistula, and much pus flowed that all went bowel and moisture from the body; and many cures were put around him for two years, and no wise man in the art of medicine was present, until I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines they used to heal him, and what ran out through the sores with great flow; and the young man's body became red, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I sewed a tent over one of the wounds, and then I searched for all the wounds, and found that some were coming towards the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 Then I hurried and dug into one of the wounds as far as I discovered part of the bone, and found it rotten and broken, and the rot was reaching the bone within; what appeared to me to be rotten bone seemed to be all there was, except for that which remained; and I began to heal the wound with medicinal salve for a long time, but could not close it; then I renewed my efforts, as before, and discovered the bone again, and found continuous rot in the bone, and removed it, and then attempted to heal the place; but I could only dig around a palm's breadth of the bone, and the wound remained open; then I healed it with medicinal salve again; and it became healthy and closed quickly, but there was no need to continue the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for my fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 Because of the evacuation, it often bleeds profusely, but it was completely healed, and a hard cyst grew in place of the bone, and it had good composition and no harm or adverse effects at all, neither inside nor outside.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated as follows: take thread, and tie it to the open end of the bone; command someone to stretch it upwards; put another thicker thread of linen over the first thread, and tie it above the corrupted cyst that is away from the bone, and hold tight so that you pull out the corrupted cyst below, and uncover the healthy cyst in the place where you want it to be, so that it does not bleed the healthy cyst; put charcoal or a plaster beneath the bone to cover the corrupted cyst; and it must be done as much as can be seen and felt, and repeated.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or a part, you must uncover all the flesh; then put iron under it, and let the softer part of the corruption be opposite to the harder part, as we have said; and if the corruption is at a joint, strike the corrupted joint and hold the bone that it contains from the other side; and if the corruption is between two joints, there is no other remedy but cutting; and if the corruption is at the end of the hand or foot, it is very difficult, but nevertheless you must investigate the corruption to see how it opens; and clean it in all the ways that you can, but be careful not to harm the vein or nerve; and know that the instruments for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bone and the appearance of the wound, and its thickness and thinness, and its hardness; and therefore, it is necessary to choose an instrument suitable for each kind of work; and know that the work will show you the tool that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the symptoms of diseases; if you think that the tool that you need depends on what it must be.
dou feu	Hot iron (or cautery)
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The head of the shoulder may burst out from within or from outside; and when you have administered that corrosive medicine for its cure, and it does not help at all, then it is necessary to cover that member up to the level where the corrosion occurs, so that the patient expires from this due to the lack of the member, or from the greater malice of the defect of the member; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, as if it were burnt by fire, and afterwards it turns black, because the corrosion of the member spreads from one member to another and takes over the whole body; hasten then to cover it, and if it is due to the sting of some venomous animals such as sea scorpions or snakes and similar, if the corrosion is at the head of the hand, cover it and do not give it any space to reach up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 If it comes up to the hand, hit at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; if it comes to the arm, strike the side; and if it passes the side, it is death, and there is no remedy except the quantity of its virtue; and thus do when the corrosion comes or breaks a bone: if it comes at the first joint, strike after the next joint; and if it comes or breaks, strike the whole bone; and if it moves in the leg, strike at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy except to tire the patient until he dies; and the way to hit or bind the member is that you tie it above and below, and stretch a servant one of the bands below, and another servant the upper band, and pull the flesh that is between the two bands apart with a large spatula, until the bone is exposed; then strike or bind, and put on both sides linen cloth so that the binding does not touch healthy skin, and causes the patient other injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	1. And when bleeding comes out while you work, then cauterize the area immediately, or apply some powder that restrains it; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the limb with a suitable ligature, and cure it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to one man in my presence: he had a blackness that resembled a burn from fire, and this corrosion came first on his foot of the leg, until it affected the entire leg; and when the man saw the corrosion, he covered the leg with a dressing, and it healed; and a long time later, the corrosion returned to his hand or to one finger, and it came to me, and I applied repercussive substances after the cleansing of the body, but the corrosion could not stop; and he asked that I amputate his hand, and I refused, for I had hope of restoring the matter; and I also feared that if I amputated his hand, he would die, for the strength of man was weak; and he despaired of all things, and returned to his earth, and covered his hand with a dressing, and it healed; and I have told this story only because one does otherwise, if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 At times an abscess occurs in the charnel place and remains for so long that it causes a large swelling of the body; then it turns and pierces, and the pus jumps out, leaving the flesh visible, just like a knight's armor; and the skin that is above is as thin as fine linen unraveled, and will not penetrate to the bone or to the nerve, and such disease is called "sain," and is not called "fistula"; but if it becomes so long that it reaches the bone entirely, it is called "fistula"; and the skin should be cut all around, just as fine linen; and it does not heal due to corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 If the skin hardens and the corruption is not complete and the skin is thick with fat, cure it with a poultice in this way: Look to see if the breasts are large and if the pores there are full of stinking odor, then apply an Egyptian-made poultice that is made like this: Take asafetida, oil, and litharge equally, cook them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey; then take some of it according to your need, make it into a water and honey mixture, and apply it to the breast, and squeeze out the pus; leave the medicine there for two hours, then drain it; do this many times until the breasts are healed and the pus is expelled; sometimes, when the Egyptian-made poultice is not available and you have no other choice but to use ashes of vinewood, pour water over them, let it cool, and apply it as a poultice, until you know that the breasts are clean; if the patient cannot bear this, or the Egyptian-made poultice or the water of vine ashes, then apply a honey and wine poultice where the honey has properties to cleanse and wash, and the wine makes the blood coagulate; when you have done this and believe that the breasts are clean, apply whatever ointment cures them, which I have described the properties or treatment of; if the openings in the breast are small and the cotton of the poultice cannot enter, widen it with a little iron, and put Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment over it so that it is widened; if the wound is too large, let it heal by itself and allow only the level or the poultice to enter; if the discharge from the breast is above, press down or press lower until it stops.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	1. When the intestine is completely protruded, do not let it hang out; and if you cannot cover the belly beneath as you see, arrange it in such a way that the intestine drops to its lowest point, because when the intestine is completely protruded, do not let it hang out and if you cannot cover the belly beneath as you see, arrange it in this manner: the intestine moves slightly downwards, and do not leave anything of the intestine; and take medicines to put on the wound, and place a linen cloth over the entire wound; then press firmly against the affected part near the hernia, and afterwards cover the hernia with another cloth according to the size of the affected area, and place it over the hernia in the wound to align the intestine, and do not remove the large cloth except after several days once; and the one who is on the hernia should often be removed to remove the hernia, and know what comes out from the hernia, whether it is poison or pus or indigestion; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been extended in this manner and you see the nature that rises on the wound of the intestine, then know that the hernia will not heal yet, and approach the healing; then unbind it in the morning or the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast becomes swollen indigest after many days, know that breasts do not shrink (atrophy).
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poison corrupts slowly, do not despair of health for it approaches health.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 And there are men whose flesh delays in healing in their wounds, and of those who do the opposite; and if he indiscreetly eats sour milk after many days, his breast will not heal; and if the breast takes a long time to swell, and is swollen, apply drying medicines that are moist in substance and dry in effect, such as oil of roses, for there is great part of vitriol, and it is the last medicine; take oil of roses, and make it with rose oil, and add equal parts of old wine in substance; then mix and use it; and the same is better when cooked and thickened, when oil of roses is not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them, and sprinkle the powder on the honey when it is over the fire; and then apply the plaster, and place it on the breast, and sometimes administer long Aristolochia root and celestial root, which is also like flour and chalk; and use simple or compound remedies: grind them, make into powder, and sprinkle on the honey that I said, and use; and if the wound is deep and not healed by this cure, know that corruption is full, and makes pressure in the bone, or in the hard members, or in the ligaments; then cure it with the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nailbed
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Parasitic abscess originates below the nail of the finger or toe, or occasionally appears in other joints; and when it is neglected, it can grow, and run along the nail root until it reaches the base, possibly damaging it entirely; and then comes the corrosion up to the bone, causing such pain that the joint becomes swollen and the color turns foul.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When treating it as we have said in the previous section and the cure does not work, you should amputate the affected part. Then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is intact; and if the nail grows into the flesh, begins to rot and blisters, you should place the iron under the nail so as not to touch the flesh, push it upwards, and gently and delicately cut the rotten tissue and remove it; then treat it with warm ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corrosion is in the bone, strike and draw it out, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see the tooth becoming corrupt, strike it in the nose as stated before, then cure it until it heals; and if it is wounded, punctured, and causes great pain, it is necessary that you drain it first; then strike the nail with the sharp probe transversely, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too great pain; and if this happens, place something to ease the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The boil that arises in some men's hands by chance is completely fleshy, and by chance it has flesh or bone, and sometimes there is a nail, and sometimes one grows from the root of the joint, where the growth occurs in some noses of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 He who is born within any knot does not remain silent; he who is born at the joint of the knot, may remain silent; the size of one who is fleshy is light in this manner: measure him by his root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	The one born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: hold it with a cover;
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one who is born or must at the last knot, it is necessary that you cut the flesh roundly up to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, then heal it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The same sores that come to the joints come together due to birth, or due to injury from a wound, or by burning with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 If you cut the suture, it must be repaired according to their natural shapes; then place between two tents or dampened cloths in oil, so that they do not adhere; or you may place between two thin pieces of plank, until the joint is healed, as necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Also, if any of its two sides comes with the palm, strike that suture as needed.
des vils	 The poor ones
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 These are large veins filled with excessive, melancholic mucus that come in many members of the body; and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk a lot and work hard, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer purges of gall and then cleanse the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The cure with iron is done in two ways: one is by striking it, and drawing out the black blood; and the other way is that you open a vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The incision is done in this way: first heat the leg with very hot water, making the flesh softened, then hold the patient's leg above the knee down to the part below the kneecap; then strike the vein in one of the three places, with a wide cut, then separate and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient's strength can bear; and then tie it up, and command him to eat food that cleanses the black bile; and repeat the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, and help the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The elevation of the haematoma is done in this manner: Rest the patient's leg, if it has much hair, then immerse it in warm water, and rub the patient's leg with hot water until it turns red and swells; and if there is no bathing water available, heat the affected area with fire. Then press towards the swelling near the knee or below the ankle; peel the skin around the swelling from both sides as it appears, so that it can be seen; and you will see it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems like a white cord. Push the head of the bone inside until the swelling is raised above the skin, then gently pull it back to the incision, then press in another place three fingers away. Peel the skin over the swelling again as it appears, lift it up as before, and press at the tip of the toe, then pull and remove it until it is all pulled out, unless you cannot pull it or lift it. If not, push a thick needle through the whole length of the cord and draw and pull it, pushing it under the bone, and turn your hand from one side to another until it comes out; make sure it does not break, as it can neither be drawn nor lifted, causing harm to the patient. When you have completely treated it, put moistened wool soaked in vinegar and oil over the wound and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the face is contracted and twisted, bent together and not straight, as we have said, then you should cut it harshly, but do not cover it; and draw [the parts] as we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron used to strike the face should be curved and not sharp, cutting the vein; it is thick, for if it is thin, it would cut the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	 From the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is located in the legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow and on dry land; but by chance it may grow elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of worms that come from under the skin as they move inside the body, penetrating between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then the limb changes color, and the vein begins to burst forth like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the head of the wound is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of plank from 6 to 8 inches long and sew it, leaving the plank on the leg, and every time it points outwards, you should wrap it again with the plank and sew; and if it is too long, cut off a part, and wrap the remaining, but do not cover its root, until it has completely burst forth; because if you cover it, it returns into the flesh, causing abscess and worms or other illness; for this reason, it must be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein when it is treated reaches a length of 5 or 10 fingers, and once it came to me, from which it burst forth 10 fingers long. When you pierce it, press a clove or garlic, and pierce it until it is completely empty; empty the matter that is inside, introduce into the wound medicines against worms every day for a while, then cure as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes in opening this vein, many times it reopens itself, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or hand and much blood flows out; then treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called "cow disease" in our land because it often appears in cattle and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, moving through the body expanding and contracting, causing pain in one limb after another until the skin or it breaks, and jumps out; it is an infestation of pus from certain humors, as serpents, larvae, worms or roundworms in the stomach come; its danger is suspected because when it moves through the body and reaches the head, and comes to the eye, it may enter the oil and destroy it; this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it to cure and drain, one can force it out only when it moves: Therefore, you must tie the place above and below with a strong cord tightly, then strike above and drag it out, and if its head is buried deep in the flesh, and you cannot find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest damage that it does, is that it corrupts oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, hold a thin spoon under it, then strike above, and drag it out; and it is necessary to use the patient for purification of body with soluble medicines for bad humors, and avoid eating spoiled foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 The pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that moves from one member to another; and I have seen this as I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was summoned to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; afterwards, I noticed it rising like a worm towards the shoulder, very quickly, just as hot silver cuts from one place to another; the pain spread from that place and pierced the shoulder, and shortly after it ran through the whole body until it came into the other arm; then she told me that it returned again around the body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how it moved from member to member, because I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 I would have wished that many had wanted to move the pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins open, and for this reason such constrained windiness appeared; and they do not appear according to this reasoning to those who are ill and have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see to cure this disease and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, lie it above and below hastily, and then press on it until the constrained windiness goes from the place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it in your eyes, cure it with those who drive out windiness, such as fetid pills and serapin pills, and similar things.
des saiettes	 arrows (or projectile points)
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are of various kinds, according to their shapes and the places in the body where they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The differences among them are that some have large points, and small, and smooth, and hinged; and some have two angles, and others have tongues, and some that have pieces; and when it falls into any member, it falls in one of the two ways: either in a principal member, like the head, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it falls into any of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you after, warns you: if you must beware of the extraction of this arrow, for the death comes in many ways after; and when this ill sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not fully in, pull it out, and care for the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the signs of the brain when an arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and a wound appears above the brain, are scotomia (blurred vision), sode (swelling or tumor), esvertin (convulsions), roujor en eulz (redness in the eyes), inflammation and redness of tongue, spasms and confusion of mind, vomiting of bile; and possibly without fever from the nose or ears; and perhaps losing speech and voice; and a white discharge from the wound resembling pus, and it may also weep like bruise of flesh; and if these signs appear to you, refrain from treatment and remove the arrow if it isn't embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The sign of the arrow when it strikes or pierces, is that it is close to the left breast, and it feels as if it has been driven into something hard, not empty; and perhaps the arrowhead also closes up like a fingernail, and in court black blood appears, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: therefore, know with certainty that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of an arrow that has not penetrated the flesh is when there is no scum coming from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, breathes heavily and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrow falls on the bed cover, it has missed the ribs; and it causes great pain and sighing, and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrowhead or stomach falls out of the wound by chance, any undigested meat may jump from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrowhead or stomach falls out by chance and anything from the intestines escapes through the wound, there is no hope for recovery nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrowhead falls into the bladder and urine escapes and leaks out, causing the patient great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the arm and neck, shoulder and joints of the shoulder, spine of the back, rib cage and thighs, legs, and limbs resembling them, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it's not poisoned, as I will tell you what happened to me, you should do this:
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 When an arrow strikes or pricks a man in the root of his nose, I pulled it out from the other side beneath the ear fat, and it was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And the pulling out of an arrow that strikes in the oil beneath the paper below (meaning under the skin), and the arrow is curved, and cannot be reached but the tip towards the bone; and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow, with all its feathers remaining; the archer was healed, and there were no ill effects.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And I pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian; it was an Arabic arrow with ears: I was the barber, and I made it as subtle as possible before pulling it out, and the Christian recovered.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And I pulled out an arrow that was lodged in a man's chest or abdomen, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change; I made a cut on the arrow, tricked it, and pulled it out without any complications.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if you see a man who has an arrow in his back and the wound is sewn shut; and the arrow remains inside for a long time without changing its natural position or causing any harm to any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And if another man receives an arrow in his face and the wound heals; and remains like that for a long time without suffering great pain, and many similar things happen.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And an arrow was shot at the prince king, who had fallen in the snow and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was completely buried. I was called to treat it after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I probed it with a thin probe and did not feel anything; but he felt pricking and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was the tip of the arrow. I placed a leech-like remedy on it that is soothing and digestive, because the wound did not swell; and the arrowhead appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I placed the plaster on his hand for several days, and healed the wound straightaway, so that the patient felt the arrowhead inside his flesh each day; and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I applied a corrosive medicine on the wound for several days until it was opened, and then probed it, and felt the head of the arrow sticking to its place; then I cauterized in the opening of the wound with that same corrosive medicine until the tip of the arrow became visible; and it healed well beyond four months, and then the wound closed up so much that I could not remove the pliers from it; therefore, I did not cease to refine and devise ways of instruments, until I made the pliers properly according to what its shape will be at the end of this chapter, as long as I pulled on it and returned the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the experts judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored; I will restore it then, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, but do not take my word for it entirely, because books cannot grasp everything; however, wise masters comprehend a small amount and the present and failing case, find nine works and new tools, to the detriment of foreign things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows do not enter the limbs where they are inserted except in two ways: either through the side or from the front; and those that burst forth where they enter are called "arrows entering into flesh," and at times they may burst forth now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not jump now, let it be until the flesh is healed around, and make the wound smooth; and similarly, if it has been driven into the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days, and move it every day; then it will jump, and if it still does not jump, perforate it all around with a fine instrument, until the surrounding areas are widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 And if the arrow is driven into the skull bone and goes up to one of the ventricles in the brain, or any of the accidents I mentioned before occur for the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it until it becomes even after several days, because if the arrow reaches so far, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not driven far beyond the bone but only reaches it without breaking, and the patient experiences some bad condition for several days, then consider drawing it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is deeply lodged and cannot be extracted, administer tourniquets as I have told you, then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 If the arrow is hidden within the body and cannot be seen, exert all your effort to find it; if you can feel it, draw it out with an appropriate instrument if possible; if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound or the depth of the arrow and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then widen the wound as much as possible; draw the arrow if you can, and if it has ears like a fishhook, remove the affected tissue on both sides as much as you can, and then bend or break the "ears" of the arrow so that you can pull it out; be careful not to break the arrow while pulling it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then lay the body down towards its joints, then pull, because the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the discharge of blood hinders recovery, bring what we have said about treatment in its chapter; and beware of incision of the nerve and vein, and provide a means to draw out the arrow safely, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the shape they were in when the arrow struck them, for this is the greatest help that can be, and if you cannot do it, put it as the signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow coming from another part, if it opens anything of it or the skin is swollen where one can see or feel it; cut then across, as far as the pliers can take hold, and then pull it out; if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If the arrowhead is lodged in the bone, turn your hand round, so it enters into the bone and expand the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.
