And if it cannot come out, leave it still and then continue the extraction until it does emerge; and if it is an arrowhead inside, push it all the way in; and if it has fallen, and you see that it needs to be administered gently, give a tool with a long handle, so that the point of the arrowhead enters the hair of the tool; then push harder, and if the arrowhead is embedded, insert the tool pointedly into it, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrowhead is touched, it is necessary to cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if the arrowhead falls in the side or the belly or the bladder or the flank, and it is near and you can cover it, do so; and be careful not to cut the vein and the nerve, then remove it, and sew up the wound if necessary; and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to extract arrows is similar to an owl's beak, as shown here:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways of doing it: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the root of the hair is also like the quill of a bird, to push at the point of an arrowhead, as shown in this figure:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for pushing and pulling is as follows here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of the common veins (of the body)
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 The number of veins from which one recovers is thirty-one, thus it has a chief sixteen, that is to say: Two batans which are after the ears, called "doubles herbech"; and the two arteries which are in the temples apparent; and the two veins which are on the cheeks of the eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that is between the eyebrows; and the vein that is at the forehead; and the two windings which are on the neck; and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these veins are called "augeherich"; and the two veins which are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly healed in every arm are V: one is cephalic, and it is situated on the left side of the chest, and the lay people call it "vein of the head"; the median is called "fast," and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the lay people call it "vein of the heart"; the basilic is located on the right side of the chest, and the lay people call it "vein of the belly," and it is above the elbow, and it is the one from which blood is drawn, which opens obviously above the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 The cubital and ulnar are the veins that are between the ulna and the little finger; it has two rain-like branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is beneath the wrist on the left side of the chest, and the second saphenous vein which is at the right ankle; and the vein called "nase," which is at the other ankle's wrist; and in the other leg there are three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The sick person should help the drainage of veins that are behind the ears with ancient cathartics and emetics; and the quality of draining, as I tell you, is to seize the head of the patient, and rub the place or the veins with a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck with a screw, until the two veins appear behind the ears in the two places depending on the head; then press down where you feel the pulse beneath your hand, and seize it; then take the lancet and push it through the vein until the bone, then move your whole hand up the entire vein, pierce and the skin and the vein well twice through, and make the blood come out until you see; then tie and hold it, until it is healed; and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The first artery of the two in the temples, is useful to treat migraines, scrofula and chronic otitis media; and its properties are as I say: and it is that the patient tilts his neck so that both veins appear clearly; and you feel a pulsation under your thumb, then press on it; then lift the skin above the vein towards your head, insert the lancet, lift the vein and squeeze, as you have done in other veins, and draw the blood according to your need; then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on it; and then form a knot and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about its closure and its extraction, where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The following of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the incision of the skull for diseases of the face of olden times, and it has migrated and turned red; and its qualities are that the patient tilts his neck while turning, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose shape is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, allowing the blood to flow according to its quantity that you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein when it is healthy and never use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flames should not be too sharp; and the vein should be pierced transversely, as the bone is near, and in case the flames are too thin, they might break when they are too fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The incision of the two veins that are in the eyes helps with inflammation, swelling, turning red, pain in the eye, and diseases of the face; and its qualities are that the patient tilts his neck while turning to one side, as before; then heal it, and make the incision across, a short distance from the flame, but wide enough because there is no charcoal.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, they may break; then make the wound bleed, as much as needed, and then cover it with linen, and hold it in place.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The vein of the nose in the nostril is useful for headaches, scrofula (chronic infection of the lymph nodes), and diseases caused by heat, such as migraines and redness that occur in the face, especially when it is old; and the quality of the vein is that the patient stretches their neck, then holds their nose with your left hand, takes fine, long flame, and pierces it between the two nostrils, since the nose does not open easily at first, and the blood will begin to flow soon; do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to necessity, then let it rest for a night, since it is quickly restored; this is the form of flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The first guinea pig's bile helps in the tightening of the anus, at the beginning of the process of healing, and with many diseases, inflammations, corrodings, herpes, and ulcers; and the quality of the bile is that the patient strains his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and the master being above the patient's head, and the patient lies on the bed, then he opens the vein from one end a little widely, then draws out the blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then he does the same in the other vein, then unties the ligature, and gently tightens all the veins so that the patient does not strain; and leaves it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	 From the surgery of livestock
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	For the purging of the veins in the lips above, it helps for coughing in the mouth, and for the corruption of the gums, and for cracks in the lips, and for the toothache and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of surgery are to have the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I said; then turn the jaw, and look at the two veins, one on the right jaw and the other on the left, and these can be recognized by their being black, and by small veins surrounding them: therefore grasp both, and if you do not know which ones they are, or if you are in doubt, grasp the larger of each, and do the same with the upper and lower veins, for it is the same way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 From surgery under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The surgery of the veins under the tongue helps after the cephalic surgery, and it is in the throat constriction, and with eye diseases, and mouth diseases; and the qualities of a surgeon are that the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and he licks his tongue, and looks below on each side for a black vein: therefore grasp one and the other, and do not go too deep, because underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins that are commonly healed follow two methods: either by pricking them deeply with a broad iron needle or with a thin olive-oil type syringe, as you call it, and they are called "anesil"; and they are large and thin according to the size and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirtin is very famous, and is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 It is necessary to open hairless large veins that contain a large amount of blood and are turbid; this is the shape of the olive-oil syringe.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and subtle, for cleansing thin veins with subtle blood or yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The healing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with the diseases that are under the neck, throat, breast, and stomach; it is necessary for the patient to heal correctly and to empty the artery that is underneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 If it touches the artery and bleeding occurs, it must be stopped, as I said; but the flame should not be pricked, but rather cut like a needle.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 If the bladder does not open manifestly, it must be opened, and change another if you wish any relief from it or it becomes sick in its place, the vein opens manifestly; and strike the flame with a needle as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you want to know the place of the pain, then you must press the arm until you feel the pulse; then mark its location and bind the arm; strike the vein with the flame like a needle; be careful not to wound the artery when you see it swelling, for it is the artery; avoid that then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it rise high like a child's urine and the wound is red and thin, know that it is not from an artery: therefore, hurry up, and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger when the bleeding stops; leave the arm like that, and do not move it; let the patient be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound does not stop bleeding and the medicine is not present, stop the artery if it is open, for the head of the limb will retract; stop the bleeding from the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 Take a bark of fumitory and cut it in half, and place one half on top until the next day; if it stops bleeding, that is good; if not, cure it as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and stopping the bleeding should not be overdone due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The vein in the middle helps to drain blood from both above and below, as it is made up of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and the physician should pierce it along the nerve that is underneath, but if he pierces too deeply and finds the nerve, and inflates it and the patient becomes sick or injured, and there is a possibility that it cannot heal; and this nerve often opens up multiple times, and if it does not open in any men due to its subtlety, you must cauterize it with the instrument. And pull out the nerve to your ability.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The vein of the head helps to drain blood from both above and below, and aids in healing wounds; and it is necessary to pierce with olive oil or myrtle fire, as this is the safest of all veins, as there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Therefore, one must seek the easier joint, and not to worry if it is necessary for the first time, and we try again; and perhaps the joints swell in some men when it is necessary for the first time, but do not worry about it.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound, according to your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you should know about bloodletting is that it should not be performed except to maintain health and to prevent future illnesses; and bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins: the cephalic, the femoral, or the basilic; and bloodletting should be done at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and bloodletting should be performed on the first day or the third day, three hours or four days afterwards.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The treatment for illnesses is not determined at any specific hour, but it should be administered whenever necessary, day or night, in all hours and at every moment; and it is not appropriate to treat children under the age of 14, nor women during pregnancy except for the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	It is not necessary to cleanse those who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 When someone wants to be treated, in whatever way that may be, it is necessary that their intestines are cleansed with a light enema, if they have retained much gas, so that the veins do not carry away the waste products and harm the main organs; one should not treat those who are very salty from foods, drunk, or overly exhausted, as long as they are still intoxicated; nor should one treat those suffering from colic pain, vomiting, stomach disorder, excessive appetite, and excessive sexual activity, hard work, staying awake, and fasting, and those whose vitality is depleted, either due to the weapon or the body itself; then refine the humors, if they are not too thick, with foods and drinks and medicines, if you have that power; then bathe, unless anything prevents it, to thin the blood, and treat the vein on the left side from the third one down, as we have said; and keep that day free of work, pain, lust, and similar things; be patient and joyful, and let the healer be above the one being treated, and rub their arm two or three times, then gently loosen the ligament on top, for when it is too tight or too loose, it cannot heal itself; then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell, and feel them; then moisten the healer's finger with a little old oil, then put his right hand's thumb on that vein under the area where one wants to treat, so that the vein does not flee and fail when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 For there are veins that run like cords in the body, and some of these are full of pus, so that when fire is applied, it shrinks away from the flame and cannot open the vein, and such is the case with some; and if the vein opens, the wound is too narrow, which requires that the person who does this should be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, that is good; but if not, continue again under that place or near immediately, unless the wound is inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 If the limb is swollen and the patient fears, leave it for a day or two, do not tie the arm: perhaps pus will come out; do not immerse it in water, then repeat the cautery if you wish; and if the hole is small, or the wound is shallow and you doubt that there is much blood, apply the fire directly to the hole itself; and open it a little hastily, so that the limb swells again; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the limb swelling, do not start draining it immediately, but put a little oil of lard on it, for it alleviates the body from blood, and the oil is solidified in that place; and thus administer the oil of lard in each wound to stop the flow of blood; and this same oil also serves as a plaster and poultice when applied to the limb; if it becomes too thick, it becomes fine and spreads when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 If a large abscess occurs, which often happens when the wound opening for vein draining is small, act quickly, and put hot, wet sponge on the limb and press it for an hour; then you should do this after the flow of blood from the vein, and if it remains at the place for some days without any black or green discoloration, it does not harm; and if you see, put something of aloes or myrrh steeped in warm vinegar, mastic, or a similar substance.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often abscess and appearance occur at the opening of the basilica: place your hand on it then, if you find the area soft under the pressure of your hand, this is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But do not apply any of the things we have said, because possibly it is an artery; but place one dry bandage to stiffen it, then treat with another cure until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	Draw blood from each (wound) according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	If the wound is black, let it drain until it turns red; if you see it swollen, let it drain until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for the one who is full and hollowed out, and requires bloodletting, to make a larger incision, and let the veins be wide; and for the weak one, do the opposite, and it should be drained little by little, and it should be drained through slicing sideways, not pricking; and this method of bleeding is safe from incorrect bleeding and nerve compression, and worth more than long bleeding rather than wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 For the one whose body needs bleeding, it is necessary to give moistened bread below the pomegranate; if he is heated, let him bleed three or four times; and for the one of cold complexion, pre-treat before bleeding with moistened bread in syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chives, and a fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if it swells in the wound, after a great flow of blood, then one must apply gruel of charcoal, and scented subtle syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If you want to burst open the arm or heal it again at another time, when it is weakened by much bloodletting, it is required that it be bled little by little according to its continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	If you want to burst open the arm after the first bloodletting and one has a strong chest, it should be bled 6 hours after the first bloodletting or the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to heal from another part, must heal by the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 For there is much blood within the body which has been heated and causes fever; then it must be drained in large quantity, and the wound should be opened wide until it swells again; then you must observe all the signs of swelling, and place your hand above the swollen part to prevent death by swelling, as this happens many times when those who drain the wounds are negligent; and it is not advisable to dislocate the arm and draw blood a second time, if the wound closes, you must press firmly; if it is curved, stretch the arm immediately, for this would be bad; but leave it until it swells again a second time; or burn the end of the arrow with the flame, so that the congealed blood from the vein flows out, and place the piece of fresh linen on top and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If the vein is burst, leave it be and do not squeeze it until the abscess has been calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If there is a need to draw blood again, then take it from the same place, or another vein, or the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are composed of many small veins.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of sainting is that the patient pushes their hand into hot water, until the flesh becomes red; then it should be tied moderately, so that the vein appears well, then it should be pricked with a lance not through wide or long holes; and large wounds should be made, and the saining should be done close to the joint of the hand, and if one cannot pull out, put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood come out in the water, as much as you have; and if it is cold, do not hit the hand with hot water again, for it puts more in winter than in summer; and saining of this vein is safer than all other veins, there being no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The hot cautery of the thumb of the right hand is effective for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done: hold the thumb, apply hot sharp fluid until the vein escapes if you can see it; and if the hot fluid goes in sideways, and if you cover it completely on all sides, it will not cause any harm; and do not immerse too deeply, as nerves are naked underneath all over, then put the thumb back in hot fluid again, but ensure that the wound is not frozen and cannot heal.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drained the blood as needed, place oil and wax on top of the vein to seal it quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The poultice on the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse, and do as I told you with the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The cautery of the vein (sophene) is effective for all diseases under the body, such as diseases of the stomach, retention of phlegm, diseases of the kidneys, and old diseases of the hips and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the quality of his health is such that the patient must put his foot in hot water and rub it on the vein until it perishes, and tie above the joint of the foot; and when the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot goes much further; therefore, bind it there or as wide as the ankle, which is more beneficial.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	If you cleanse above the foot, guard against the nerves that are below, and cleanse through it as well, in the same way as when cutting; and let the fire be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the limb cannot come out, put it into water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 If the vein needs to be bound for the first time, start again a little higher, because it is salted; do not doubt of the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the soothing of the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The thigh of the sciatic nerve is at the knee joint, and its pain resembles that of the hamstring when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the quality of his health is such that the patient immerses himself or herself in water and pulls above the ankle four fingers while twisting, for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, you should bind it in every way possible, and by crossing; it is more beneficial to cut it, because the vein is full of bile, and is greatly susceptible to humans.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you don't heal it, no medicine will open or close the side of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; let the bleeding continue as much as you see fit, then cut the ligament, put cotton on it and press; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 The wound drains pus.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or of iron, or of glass; and ventosing is done in two ways: either by wounding and drawing blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 This draining (ventosation) which is called wounding can be done in two ways: either with fire or without fire; and the draining performed by wounding and extraction of blood is performed in fourteen leagues of the body, from which one is completely in the head; and the others are in the neck; and the others in the two sides of the neck; and the wounds under the chin; and the wounds in the two shoulders; and the wounds on the shins; and the wounds in the two arms; and the wounds in the two legs; and the wounds in the two ankles; and the draining does not treat blood, unless it is small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it should never be avoided, if it is done like a wound drainage; and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from congestion, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if by necessity due to illness it is required to bleed, or by custom, we administer this each hour at the beginning of the month, or at its end, and in every case; for there are those who, when they need to be bled, have a heavy head; and those who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness in the eyes; and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue swells, and they spit blood; and there are those who think, and see by no blood and nausea and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially if it is at the end of the month, we order to bleed them after 3 hours from dawn.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The nosebleed helps alleviate headaches ... that come to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this bleeding is in lieu of cephalic bloodletting, and one with a cold constitution or diarrhea should not use it, for it does great harm to them; therefore, those who have cold head diseases or who are watchful should not do it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal themselves often become negligent, and for this reason, the bellows should be placed a little lower due to the fear of neglect.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The ventosation in the neck is in the position of the saint's jaw and basilica, and for that reason it is useful for pressing on the painful part, and for cutting the channel of the perineum, and totally, and filling; and it should be pressed gently because if it holds too firmly, it can cause obliance or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The ventosation in the neck (costelz) is useful for headaches, optalmia and migraines, strangulation, tooth root pain, and is located at the basilica joint; you must instruct the patient to press gently with his hand without pressing the artery and no bleeding should occur.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilations under the chin are beneficial for mouth diseases, tooth decay, and similar mouth illnesses; they are located at the saint sites of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilations on the shoulders are beneficial for illness resulting from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The ventosations of the costal veins are as important as three veins in the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; instruct the lord not to pierce too deeply, for the flesh is naked there and knows nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventosation that is on the rump is worth as much as emorroids from the foundation and diseases below, and it must be large, and made of iron, for it needs to draw well; and if it were too thin, it would break, causing large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The swellings of the legs open widely because they draw blood from the entire body; they cause ancient pains of the kidneys, bladder, and urinary tract, and reduce the flowers [in the body]; they are in the places of the knees and ankles, and everywhere else they weaken the body after long use, and bring pus to many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the swelling is that you first empty it, suck immediately and press hastily, move equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the place red and inflated, and open the red color of the blood; then fart, and return the swellings, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are some who have hard flesh and clear pores: it is necessary to pierce only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the flesh is thick, it is necessary to pierce twice: the first time to refine the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the bone is very thick, it should be struck three times; and when we wish to draw blood drop by drop, we must pierce only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 If we wish to draw a lot of blood, let us frequently do so; if the skin is thick, pierce deeply, and be sure that the nerves are cauterized quickly, and it is necessary for those with thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the areas of the ventosations with stimulating and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, use oil of violets, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, use oil of watercress, lily, chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	and if the superfluidity is thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the patient has to stretch tender skin and large pores, no oil should be applied, but it should be washed after ventosation with rose water, cold water, vinegar water, cucumber water, lime water or another similar substance.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And one who has much moisture, if he rises from ashes or from myrtle water and sumac and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And those with large superfluities should rise from old wine or sour milk, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or others; and it is not advisable to ventosate before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and they should not sleep after the ventosation, and it is necessary that he urinate, when he needs to be ventosed and when he has been ventosed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And be aware that if the patient who is cured is coleric and lacks sharpness and is inflamed, it is necessary that he takes cold things, such as raw pears or endives and lettuces; and similar things; and consume little, and meat of young chicken, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 If the patient has a cold constitution, let him drink syrup of honey and moderately strong-smelling wine (between old and new), consume little, and chicken breast or pigeon; on the day he is purged, he should drink more than eat; it is also necessary to give some men certain times triple or muscat before or after purging, for strengthening the main limbs; and let the body of the patient be refined, but it must not be hot drinks for him.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The cauteries with fire are to be applied to the following parts: the liver, spleen, gout, stomach and side, the groin and flank, and the loins; for these members cannot bear to be struck with iron, and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another, as we do with mammary abscesses; to remove the thick fluid in a member, as we do with ventouses on the stomach and the flank to reduce the swelling; and relieve pain, whether there is an obstruction or stone, by its attractive power it may draw out the obstruction or dislodge the stone from its place; and thus it acts when applied to the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these ventouses are administered empty for sucking only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with cold liquid, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a way one fills the ventouse with warm or hot liquid containing cooked herbs appropriate for the case.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the blister treated with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should have a width of two fingers and half a palm breadth, and have a notch around the middle, as with pushing an awl, made of bone, soft in front so that it does not prick the patient when placed on the member; and in the middle there should be a rod of bone or iron, for putting a handle in place, and they should be large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; because the tumors of children are different from those of the old, and the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And thus this tumor press should be placed on the member: take the handle of wax or linen and put it in the opening of the rod that is in the tumor, so that the light is at the bottom of the tumor so that it does not burn the patient; then place it on the member, and the fingers should be over the notch as we said, so that when one looks, if steam comes out, remove the tumor; and take the linen again as before, and repeat often, if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the bladder, which is administered in pleurisy disease, there should be neither prick nor piercing, and it should not be applied except when it is full of water, and it is placed only on the member; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Without pricks or piercings should not be applied except to members where bladders cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in places with no skin, such as the eye or nose, and others; and the quality of the user is that when you find bladders in clear, sweet water without impurities, take them; and place them in clean, sweet water until they are familiar, and have nothing in their bladder; then be incised with a vein and bladder, then rub the member until it turns red, and place the bladders on it; and when they are full and warm, if it is a place where a bladder can be placed, put it there, as this is very effective.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If the shoulder is not in place, lift it up gently, then press down strongly, and then sprinkle it with vinegar; and if the shoulders are still not well aligned too far from the body, dampen a linen cloth with cold water, put it on until the sores dry out; and if the sores multiply, apply broken vitriol or sulfur and similar things until they dry up; or you put half-peeled fava beans on the shoulder and leave them until they harden onto the shoulder, it will now stop bleeding; and if you need more help, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the sores do not want to take leeches, you scrape the shoulder with fresh blood, or you prick it with a needle until the blood comes out and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they harden; and when you see that they are bleeding again, you sprinkle some powder of aloe and of silica or ash, it will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and is about the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Inform the dear child that foolish people should avoid this chapter, for they never saw any of the old books or read any letters in them; and because of this, knowledge is alien to our land, for I have never found anyone good at it except through the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the subject and by experiment, and by the practice of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments presented, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore we shall now say the prologue of this book, the sums of the words and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and dwell on truth so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 When fracture or dislocation or twisting or swelling occurs in anyone, it is necessary that you clean the patient from both sides, unless something prevents you, such as weakness of body, or infants, or the elderly; or if the time is not very hot or too cold; and do not eat cold foods, such as raw fish and mutton, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill oneself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about abscess heating or expansion of matter in the member; if the patient returns to its first natural management, he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones start to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with foods that make good nourishment, or he has viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and meat of veal, beef, head, feet, pancreas, fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For by great nursing, the wounds are made worse and break more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that the bones broken in old or weak people cannot be well restored nor healed according to their nature due to the looseness of limbs, nor those who are too tender, like infant's bones; but do not worry, set on the broken bone the large splints that hold and join the limb together, as much as possible, so it enforces it as it was before; and provide no movement at all to it, and for this reason, feed him with coarse foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the neck is other than the break of the foot or of the leg; and I will tell you in this chapter all ways of break.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There are breaks that heal on their own without setting, and others that need to be set in the manner of cutting the feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with an open wound, or a fracture with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each way should have its tool and instrument for restoration, according to what comes to mind in its place; and fractures of the bone are known by the fact that the joint is twisted, and it opens well through dislocation, and strikes with pressure from hand; and when there is no twisting or touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no breakage; but it may have twisting or fissure, or small fractures.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not right that you move [the dislocation] with your hand, but put on medicines that come afterwards, and then hold it gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the fractures that go into the joint, and are the two parts disjointed, they should now be put back together equally, so that abscesses do not grow there; and if abscesses grow there, leave it for some day until the abscess is calmed down; then place it equal to the bone that you can easily and wisely move; and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restorations of where there are pieces; then pull, as required below.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if there are fractures in the bone with pieces, separating it into two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or at your hand a small member, or two tendons, or one tendon and at your hand; place the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, reset them by all means with additions in their places as you can, and be careful that through your work there comes no injury nor pain to the patient; align well the two joints of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with the hand if it seems to you that it is not good: straighten it carefully, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who bring it by their work abscess hot and contraction to the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is set, carefully restrain the patient so that it does not move, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and ensure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 If it feels no pain, then it is not set, and you must put it in a position so that it feels no pain; ensure that it is straightened, lest twisting comes when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs can be various in smallness, size, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For small members, such as fingers and toes: you must wrap them with soft linen cloths; and for larger ones, such as thighs and legs: you must wrap with a large, stiff rope, because the thick ropes bind the whole large member evenly, and tighten it all equally, so that there is no swelling; then tie light strips of linen or cloth around it three or four times according to the limb, and tighten your hand slightly on the entire rope, then go above the break and tighten less, than the break, then move away a little from the break; and soften the rope little by little, so that you take a large part of healthy flesh; then take another rope, and twist around it in reverse over the broken limb; then return to the lower part of the break, and tighten slightly, not too much nor too loosely, as we have said in the first place above; then put linen or cloth strips between the ropes, until they are all equal, then cover everything with a bandage, and then make your splints well, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is swelling or abscess, place something calming for the abscess on top of it and remove the swelling; leave it thus for some days; then press on your elbows, and they should be about half the width of a thick cane, or of a rod used to make clefts, or of palm branches, and they should be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 And the elbows that one places on top of the fracture should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and they should also be as long as necessary for the limb, whether it is small or large; then press on the elbows in the same way as you did in the first instance, then tie a bandage over them, just as you did with the fracture in the first instance; tighter here, and less there; and the bandage should be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax; because if the bandage is thick, like those who make their bands from twisted flax ropes, which is a great error, as the bandage cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it should not have less than double the space between each elbow.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is gored by the heads of arrows after being stretched out in healthy places, place linen or woollen cloth over them to prevent bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is broken and the vessels ruptured, I will tell the cure after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to set arrows in all broken limbs immediately on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.
