Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, remove the bandages, because you will find the bones even, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two [bones] are broken, restore them as we have said for the bones in the hand; then place a splint on the broken bone according to the length of the bone, and it should be a bit larger, then place beneath it the flat piece that I mentioned, and hold it in position; and if there are two or more, or more, break each bone, place a splint on each bone covered with one linen cloth, and hold the flat piece beneath the bone; and let it remain above the head of the flat piece facing the abdomen of the bone, so that it covers it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I said about other fractures, when we have spoken of them; and treat each case according to its necessity.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone in the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of the womb is broken, make it swell by applying heat, then incline it towards the small of the back and hold it from behind; fill the nature of the patient with cotton and place a large pad over it; then turn the woman, lift her hips slightly, and pull on the pad until it reaches the entrance of the womb, and the bone returns with the pad; when she wants to urinate, remove the pad, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for 7 days or more: the break will heal, and if you see, take a bladder of barley straw, attach a tube to one end, and blow into the other end until the straw is swollen inside; the bone will return to its place; then fill with cotton, and leave it for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the thumb in a man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the wrist-bone; and these nearby breaks are not concealed from him who puts his study and practice into it and reads my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 The broken bone signifies various positions for the correct path of restoration; therefore, let us discuss it further.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, put a goose's gullet around it, then wrap cloths around it and leave for 3 days or more, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	With break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for him who has a break with wound, especially if it is large such as the bones of the leg or shoulder or similar, that it be cauterized now, so that the cauteries which we have said bear witness to its healing.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, anoint it with vinegar, if you have none, then begin to restore the break in the same hour, or the next day, if abscess pus does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscess pus comes, wait until the ninth day, until the pus is calmed, and do not touch it for three or four days, because you will cause bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks and appears exposed at the edge of the wound, you should set it gently with your hands to a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the fracture is not aligned for you to set it evenly with your hands, you should align it with this instrument made of iron, which has 7 or 8 inches in length, and the width according to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the mirror that he takes hold of 3 or 4, according to what is required in each treatment of fracture; and it should be round and slightly larger than needed, so it does not fold under pressure on the member in your work, and sharp before, and large from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called the "wrist-bone", so the crooked shoulder should be placed over the visible bone; and push it once until it returns, and make sure they are even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the break is subtle and the instrument cannot grasp the bone well, then you must saw the head of the bone until the instrument has enough power to hold it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, strike it with an appropriate instrument, either chisel or saw, to your ability; then carve away the part that remains in the bone with sharpness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 Keep it in its place, then moisten the cloth with black stiptic wine if it is hot and do not put any oiled cloth or anything else on the wound that could cause pus or corruption; afterwards administer splints when you have restored the bone, leave the wound uncovered, cover it as necessary according to the size of the wound, take care not to strain the wound with the break; many times the foolish physician has done this and brought harm upon the patient or death or sometimes rottenness; and let the bandage be softer and more flexible than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad event may come, as we have said, and you feel pain at its place, do not put stitches on it; but wrap around it, in place of stitches, hard bandages and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one or two days that the bandage has become soft at the wound, take off what you put on and apply healing ointment for wounds, like tetraformula ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the member twice a day, at morning and evening, as long as it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be set in such a way that the bone protrudes slightly downwards gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If it passes many days and the bone cannot heal but rather protrudes again, as you know there are small fragments of bone, for this reason, it is necessary that you try to press the wound, and remove all those dislocated fragments that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 If a fistula or any form of corruption comes at the place, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what it says in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 If the bone is broken and opened on the limb, like the bone of the leg or shoulder, and other similar large bones, do not pull it out, because many times death comes, but leave it until it can set; perhaps it will heal by itself after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can; if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The buboes (swellings caused by infection) coming upon the sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Often times after the breaking of health, it happens especially near the joint, and it is a sight to behold the appearance of the limb; and by chance, the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, take care if it is fresh: administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sycamore bark, acacia, and similar others, either taking one of these things or all together, and grind them with sharp vinegar or egg white or honey; then place the mixture in a stoppered jar, strain it well, and do not let it out for many days; then drain it, and start another, until the swelling is gone; or you can use a well-made piece of plank, as the property of the plank is that it removes all inflammation from the limbs. If the swelling has turned into hardness like stone, it needs to be removed, either by chopping it off, and making the excess apparent; or you can shave it, until it is removed, and heal it when it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed and remains afterwards, the limb becomes weak and delicate for several reasons: one reason being that it was tied too tightly, but not sufficiently as required; or because there were too many ligaments, preventing nourishment to reach the limb; or due to excessive soaking; or due to excessive movement at the wrong time; or due to a lack of blood in the body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	The treatment is to have the patient eat well and make his body lean, until the blood multiplies within him; administer baths and give joy and comfort; then apply tar to the limb so that the tar attracts great nourishment, and soak it often with cold water, until nourishment reaches the limb; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after being restored and the bones are broken open and the shape of the limb is disfigured, do not believe the foolish who say that one should break the limb anew and many fools have done this in our land; and this practice is condemned, and it brings great harm, and possibly death. However, if the swellings and torments are fresh, it is necessary that they be treated with warm water or softening herbs such as vismalve leaves, roots, medlots, and similar things; and you make a soothing poultice, like dyaquilon well made, and take musk root of vismalve and mix it with ginger oil or sesame oil, and make a poultice on top; or you take fat figs, grind them with wheat bran, and similar medicines that alleviate the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes the dislocation is removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 Bring movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is enlarged and hardened, as a stone, and it requires iron removal, it must be covered up to the bone, making an incision with a subtle, delicate knife; and put cotton and bandage in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in anyone, it must now be returned without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if you wait, the joint swells, and in case it is reset again at the same place; therefore, it should not be moved when swollen: many times this brings spasms and other pains; however, when this happens, let the patient purge, then rest, until all abscesses are calmed; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then gently straighten it, and treat each member as the cure comes in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations of the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It seldom happens that the jawbones are dislocated in both places, and dislocations of both occur in two ways: either they are partially displaced from their place and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the side, and the saliva flows from the mouth which it cannot hold, nor can it close its mouth, and wraps its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a small dislocation returns through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 If it is whole and complete, then you must quickly reset it without delay; and in this manner that the servant holds the head of the patient, and puts a thumb of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; and the other hand should be spread out, to make it even; and command the patient to soften its jaws and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mirrors [should be "patient"] align it [the dislocation] evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the jaw bones are dislocated together, warm them with hot water and oil, moving them gently; do not force them, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they (the dislocated joints) are put back in place, and the patient's mouth is closed well with soft linens sewn into a purse made of rose oil and wax, then gently tie it with several ties; let the patient sleep on his back, with his arms between two cushions so that they do not move to either side or try to force themselves, but take light food until the pains are removed, and the jawbones are healed; then eat lightly whatever one wishes, and do not strain oneself by opening the mouth to eat or drink, until the jawbones are well healed and sound.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be set correctly within an hour and are not converted to their places, fever and customary sweats come, and possibly abdominal swelling and perhaps vomiting of clear mucus.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is destruction; and many times the person who experiences this dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the collarbone
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The collarbone cannot be dislocated from its continuous connection with the chest and the breast, but it is occasionally dislocated at the end, and this can be felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is such that the patient lies down on his back and extends his arms; then press the joint firmly towards your palm, and it will return; then put on a sling and bind it; the shoulder which was dislocated toward the front cannot dislocate again; if not, and if it dislocates once, then reset it to its place, as we have said; then put on a sling and bind it, and tell the patient to rest until he is sound; in the same way, the shoulders of the back are restored when they are dislocated from their place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	When the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture and cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder can only be dislocated in three ways: one is when it dislocates at the joint below the socket, and the second is at the joint of the hip; it occasionally dislocates above the joint, but this happens rarely; it does not dislocate behind the shoulder nor inside the nerves; it often dislocates below the socket towards the hip, especially for those with little muscle strength, as it can happen quickly; for those with enough muscle strength, it jumps up slightly and goes back in slightly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, happens to some men percussion or fracture, and inflames the shoulder with an abscess hot, and thinks that it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must verify it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known that the dislocations are towards the hip and distinguish between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them; and at the top of the shoulder, you will find a hollow, and below the hip near the shoulder tip, as if it were an eye socket; and the patient cannot bring his hand to its place nor make any movements; similarly, if it is dislocated above, it is not hidden, for you can feel it clearly at the shoulder tip; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to fix when it is new, unless the patient is weak.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The manner is that the servant lifts the patient's hand upwards, then puts your thumbs under the elbow, and forces the joint upward to its place; then the servant lifts the hand, and extends it upwards, put it back in place; it will come out quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said in many days, the patient should be bathed in hot water; and apply softening and soothing balm, such as decotion of elder and fenugreek and melilot in water, and apply it; then lay the patient on his back, and place a piece of linen equal in size but not too soft nor too hard under the affected shoulder, then place the heel of the person on the piece of linen, and lift the head of the shoulder carefully, and pull the arm of the patient; and another person should hold the head of the patient so that it does not move downward; that shoulder will immediately return to its original position, and if you notice that it dislocates in this way: and make sure there is someone present who is larger than the patient; and straight towards his side, push the affected shoulder under the patient's affected shoulder, and lift the patient's affected shoulder upward, so that the patient hangs on the crossbar; and another person pulls the patient's arm downward towards his stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too light, one cannot perform any weighty action with him, for the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 It is also done in another way: one pierces the long thorn into the ground so that the head is as round as a pea, neither too thick nor too thin; then it should be placed under the patient, but with wool underneath to protect him, and the patient should lie down straight on the staff; then his hand should be extended across from the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; if it does not want to return due to all the things that we have said, do this cure: take a large-thick tiron with a four-inch wide base, which has a rounded tip to enter fully into the wound, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then place the head of the tison on the sick man's joint, so that it does not burn the patient, then put it into the joint of the sick person; extend one arm above the tison, and hold the shoulder above the tison, and the hand at the end of the arm, then place the arm on a wooden wedge of a width equal to four fingers, and stretch out the other hand downwards, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will be reset immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, however it may be, you must put a cloth equal to the joint underneath the joint, then apply a plaster made of milled powder, with incense and egg white all over the shoulder and around, then hold it under the joint as it moves, and twist the thread around the plaster, and bind the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it must be eaten little by little, as long as the members are comforted, for it will heal more quickly; and afterwards eat more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is closed up and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture or for some other reason, you must administer three cauterizations as stated in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all this and it dislocates again after 7 days, and the joint cannot hold, and the arm above cannot be lifted, then understand that the nerve at the base of the shoulder is cut or stretched or weakened; and understand that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the hip or the backside is made by force and extension of hands, and another instrument is used for it; treat it until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing, the member has pain and sluggishness in movement, the patient should take baths many times until the pain subsides and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation cost   (This line doesn't make sense as it is, the translation provided above suggests that "de" is a preposition in this context but "dislocation" is a noun and it should be translated as "of the dislocation". However, "coute" seems to be missing from the sentence. The original text might be incomplete or missing information.)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the thigh is dislocated at points, and it dislocates at points again; if it has been dislocated in all directions, both front and back, and dislocation cannot be corrected because it can clearly be seen and felt, as each dislocation displaces according to its shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the healthy bone with the sick one, make sure you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it should be reset in such a way that abscesses do not come where the joint is, because if abscesses come where the joint is, it would be difficult to set; and perhaps it cannot be completely reset from all sides, especially when it is at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and possibly death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such, when it can be brought back to its place, that you extend your hand to your two hands; and his arms should be spread out, and his hands around the mirror as necessary, above and below, and push the jointure towards their peaks together, or to the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	If the dislocation is in front, then return when you bend your hand to your hand, and press from the root of the palm on the dislocated side.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 If it does not return to its place, administer strong extension; and it is that two people should extend the arm and hold it still during the extension; then turn the arm on both sides, when you have rolled up a double-length and wide cloth; and when the person puts his hand on the joint, oil it for softening the joint, then push the joint firmly until it returns; and when it is in its place, apply dry plaster with egg, and hold it firmly, and let the arm hang from the neck of the patient for several days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is closed in its place, remove the bandage and leave it; if you see that the joint is not holding well, renew the plaster and the bandage, leaving it in this state for some days until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if it feels pain after the resetting of the joint and it swells, bathe and rub it well, and press until it is soothed; or you put a sheep's wool on the jointure, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, let it enter water; and when it bleeds, rub the jointure gently, then replace the wool, and then enter it into water again; and do this two or three times until it is healed; and if you see, put warm damp sheep's wool on it, and apply pressure; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand's joint, and its reset is easy compared to other jointures; it must be returned to its place promptly, in the same hour when it is dislocated, unless the ligaments are inflamed, or there comes an abscess hot.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the resetting of the hand, you put the sick hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and align the hand, so that it is placed with the palm above the appearance of the jointure, and push until it goes back into place; it is necessary that you observe whether it is properly in position; then have the patient put the back of his hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's hand on the table, and the observer should put his hand above that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, it is good; if not, hold down the plasters that soothe abscesses with heated irons and let it heal on its own.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if it cannot be endured and you cannot put it back after some days, the dislocated joint remains twisted; and it does not harm the patient for as long as his hand is injured and he cannot exert any force: therefore know that the nerves are cut, or arteries; there is no other means except to straighten through cautery in the case, and perhaps nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is injured, place it in the plaster that we have mentioned, then stretch and leave for 5 days, then remove the bandage and leave as such.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot move well and there is no swelling, apply warm water and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on either side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the belly; then you push the dislocation towards your pockets until it returns, then hold the head of the finger and turn it towards the part where it is disjoined; and leave it for two days, and then make it even on that day; and bind it, as we have said, and loosen the binding for a day, and make it move, and bind it again; and do this often, until it is tight, and similarly do, if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done above, until it heals; and similarly do, when it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	And also do the same for the dislocation of the backbone in the spine.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the backbone in the spine or neck is dislocated, or there are many dislocations, there is no cure for it, as death quickly comes to the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are that the hernias leap voluntarily, cannot be held, and many times the member becomes softened, or in the two legs or the two arms or the neck; many times the spleen becomes silent in four parts; this which becomes silent at the rear is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you observe if the gilbositez has come from childhood: if it has not had any treatment or healing since.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And that which has fallen out or from blows or similar things, the ancient methods of cure spoke in large words, but there was not much benefit in all cases; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the swelling that comes before, there is no trick or health; and similarly, the one that comes directly between the two sides, and cannot be cured except by the one who comes from behind, as I said; and it is that the patient lies extended on his face in one place, and has a bandage under him, so that he does not bleed; then insert the needle into the main wound on the ground, and another at the feet, and tie a rope over the patient's body, and another at the hips, and knees, and ankles; and two attendants know the ropes, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two needles; and they should be well tied, the needles as we have said, and the healer places his hands on the spine erect until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return by this cure, take a table three arms long and hollowed out beneath, and the patient should be on their side; and push the head of the table underneath the opening, then place the middle part of the table on the spine; and put mirrors on each end of the table, and press hard, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it on the pulley that rotates by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And then you stick two needles in the head of the patient with one arm's length apart, and between each needle, have a space of palm width; and in each needle have a hole, or let the pulley move, and ensure the needles are firmly in the ground so they do not move; and between the two needles have a rotating needle, like liens, and have in the two rotating needles two small needles with palm width length, to turn the pulley; then tie the rope that is among the handles to the pulley towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet at the other pulley, and each of the assistants turns their pulley to the entire rope, and the master ensures the spine is level as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it [the shoulder] is in alignment, place a drying plaster containing much egg white on it, then press it, then place the rod of a three-foot table, pressing the dislocated area and the healthy part of the vertebrae, then tie a cord around it as we have said, and use the patient with gentle manipulation until it is healed; and if anything comes at the end of the healing process, administer softening and soothing medicines, with the rod mentioned above; and sometimes a piece of plank is administered, and sometimes the appearance comes at the back vertebra of the spine, and it is believed that this is dislocation; but it is the bone that opens, for which reason there should be no presumption: perhaps death will come.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the neck and the shoulder come undone only by dislocations, not in any other way; and the joint of the neck is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and it dislocates more on the inside, and less so in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer and the sick person's knee joint is more open than the healthy one; and the sick person cannot bend their knee in fire; and it is the joint that is displaced swollen with abscess hot, because the head of the shinbone comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who it comes to flee, is that this event is contrary to those mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him whose leg it is in front, are that it should be well aligned according to the completion; however, do not double the knee with pain, and if you want to make it walk, it cannot go forward, and retains its urine, and swells the ankle, and when it goes, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him whose back it is, are that he cannot extend his knee, nor bend it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hip of the thigh is at the place beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The re-alignments of this kind of dislocation are that you examine if the dislocations are old and remain in their position without treatment; no treatment should be assumed for them, nor should there be any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	In the case of fresh dislocations, which are of four types of dislocation, hurry and try to re-align the joint and push it inward and outward, moving it from side to side; by chance if it returns, no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare a strong minister and hold the leg firmly between his hands or with a rope tied above the knee; another minister should extend his hand in such a way that he pushes his hands beneath the shins, then tightens a strong rope around the shin; another person holds the head of the rope; and all extend upwards and downwards together at once, so that the patient is raised from the ground once and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to four similar situations, and if the dislocation returns as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If the joint is not in place, treatment is required for its appearance. When dislocation is at the front, you must remember to lift the patient on their unaffected side, then tie a rope around the thigh's root and the dislocated area under the angle, then pull the rope up towards the angle and towards the forceps; then take another attendant with their arms, embrace the large thigh of the affected limb, and extend it outwards; the joint will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot secure it in this manner as we have said, then you must tie the two feet of the patient tightly with a strong rope around both ankles and knees, and the affected leg should be extended two fingers more than the others; then hang him by the head from a pole, and suspend two long arms above ground; then command one attendant to embrace the top of the thigh, and let another attendant hold the patient while embracing the thigh in turn, as the joint will return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is out of place, the patient lies down, as we said in the one with gout, and pulls the ligament above the affected leg properly, and also above the foot; then put two splints, one at the top and the other at the feet, then insert the splint between the knees of the patient in the appropriate position; and wrap it with moistened cloths so as not to burn the patient, then extend each assistant towards him, and the mirrors adjust his hand equal to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If it does not return, place him on a bed and press as we said in the case of gout, and let the patient lie down on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	When the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the affected leg quickly, and as I have said; place the patient's pain on the opposite side, then press with the other hand and pull it back towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is to the outer side, it should not extend the patient downwards nor raise up on the earth, but rather it should remain as if the hip was dislocated to the outer side, as we have said in bed position on both hips; and it should be on his back, and the leg extended as we have said before, and must press upon the jointure on the table; and he will be at rest when the patient extends his legs and they are even; then align the thighs, and place the bolster, and bind with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and rest for three or four days, then unbind, and place the bolster again; and if you see that they are even, bind again as before, and let it rest for three days; then unbind, and make him walk well when the limbs are comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation at the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in four ways: inside and outside, behind; it should not be dislocated in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not bend at the knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his thigh, and place his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your hands, pull it between your hands, then bend the two sides of the knee together; another assistant extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the signs are that it bends easily at the knee lightly; apply the poultice, and hold the leg to the thigh, and let them heal together firmly for three or four days, then release it; do not let the patient walk until the limbs are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not at its proper place, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of dislocation, until it is sound.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes crushed, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it tends towards the part where it is dislocated: the repositioning should be gentle, and it should be gently extended to its hands when it has been loosened only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is completely dislocated, you must make the patient sit straight, and hold the leg by the ankle with one hand above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then to the left hand twice, then lift the foot up, and push the foot up hard; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, start again, for it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, lay the patient on his back on the ground, and fix the splint firmly in the ground between his knees, and wrap bandages around to prevent the patient from bleeding; then hold the leg by one hand, and another person holds the foot at the ankle or the shin, so that it lies above the ankle of the foot; then each person should extend equally, and the splint should be close between the knees of the patient to keep the patient still when he is lifted; then the mirrors place their hands equally on the dislocation, and another person holds the leg straight below, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is ready, place the plaster and wool on top of it, and press firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the ankle, so the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligature softens, tighten it again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and let the patient walk for four days; and if he goes before that term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess swells there, you must drain it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	the two (hands)
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both hands are dislocated, they must be carefully stretched out without strain, and it is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the dislocation is in any way between the back of the foot and the ankle, you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or bed straight up, and put your foot on top of where the joints open, then press firmly on the foot until it aligns; and when it is even and there is no gap, place two fingers under the sole of the foot, then tighten it, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and let him rest until he recovers.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with dislocation and it is to be restored, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the cure, unless you are wise in the art and have long used it, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, but not rash; and first use soothing medications on the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, reset the limb to its place, provided that the abscess soothes itself; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing medications to the abscess and treat the wound as required, using cauterized ointments; and if there is a fracture with dislocation, and small bones are dislocated, set them, and do as we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering into fear, as I have said, for this will harm you according to your Creator, and for the sake of the knowledge of your weapon and body.
Amen	 Amen (In the name of God)
